Japanese Finance Minister Explains to Cabinet Meeting; Budget Formulation Policy; Avoid Issuing More Public Bonds; Maintain Fiscal Balance 72

(Tokyo) – Today's regular cabinet meeting was held at the Prime Minister's official residence from 2 PM. Prime Minister Okada and all cabinet members attended. First, Finance Minister Takahashi read the budget formulation policy for the next fiscal year (Showa 11th year) and explained it in detail. Minister of the Army Hayashi, Minister of the Navy Osumi, Minister of the Interior Goto, Minister of Agriculture Yamazaki, and other cabinet members all asked questions to the Finance Minister, who answered them one by one. The entire cabinet unanimously approved the formulation policy, and the meeting adjourned at 4 PM. (Nichi-Ren telegram, 25th)

(Tokyo) – Now that the budget formulation policy for the next fiscal year has been decided, Finance Minister Takahashi believes that it is necessary to inform the entire nation of the actual state of national finances. Therefore, after the cabinet meeting on the 25th, he announced the main points in the form of a talk, as follows:

(1) The amount requested by each ministry each year easily reaches a huge sum of 2.8 billion or 2.9 billion yuan, and the new requests amount to a large sum of 1.3 billion or 1.4 billion yuan. However, the current financial situation is that the tax revenue is 800 million yuan, and the total ordinary revenue is about 1.4 billion yuan. It is clear that a financial system of this level cannot accommodate such large demands. (2) It is unavoidable to continue issuing a large number of public bonds next year. We cannot help but make such considerations. The issuance of a large number of public bonds began in Showa 7th year. The planned issuance quantity reached a maximum of 930 million yuan in Showa 8th year, then decreased to 881 million yuan in Showa 9th year, and further decreased to 771 million yuan in Showa 10th year. On average, it decreased by about 66 million yuan each year. There are many reasons why the current issuance of huge public bonds is relatively unhindered. The main reason is that the total budget has not expanded dramatically since Showa 8th year, and the number of newly issued public bonds has gradually decreased. Therefore, public trust in finance and public bonds has been maintained, which has been of great help. The number of new public bonds issued next year is aimed at the natural increase in revenue in the Showa 11th year budget, so the quantity is planned to be less than the new issuance number in the Showa 10th year budget. However, this plan is by no means to reduce the total budget. (3) Special accounting has recently increased due to economic recovery. The majority of the increase in revenue is distributed more to special accounting than ordinary accounting. However, its expenditure is not as much as ordinary accounting, because there are few special burdens increased due to national defense costs and other current situations. Therefore, special accounting should have considerable surplus, so new expenses can still be accounted for. Looking at the entire national financial situation, appropriate methods must also be considered regarding adjustments. The specific policies will be discussed with relevant parties after further research. (4) Each ministry should consider the overall financial situation and show concessions by mutually allocating their financial resources, regardless of territorial boundaries. This is what we hope for. (5) In view of the current financial situation, the number of personnel stipulated by officials must not be increased, and other expenses for promotions will not be reissued. This is especially hoped for. Officials must serve the public with sincerity and be consistent with the country. They should all show a spirit of opening up difficult situations and take the lead in setting an example, which is most important. (Nichi-Ren telegram, 25th)

International Commercial Telegram –Special Commercial Telegram of Reuters on June 25— 80

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 141 shillings and a halfpenny, up one penny.

British Silver: The London silver market continued to fall today. The spot price is 31 pence 0625, the futures price is 31 pence 2225, both down four-three-seven-five. Chinese bankers bought in and then sold out. India sold out, and the United States bought in. The closing market was volatile.

US Silver: The New York silver market opened and futures prices fell by about 135 pounds sterling due to the decline in prices in London and Bombay.

Indian Silver: The decline in the Bombay silver market yesterday was due to many parties correcting their position of buying too much and closing out a lot. It seems that the United States only buys silver when the price falls, and not like before, when it also bought silver when the price rose. The bulls were disappointed, and the silver price fell.

Exchange Rate

British-American: The London foreign exchange market had good trading this morning, but the US dollar and gold coin five points were down one-two compared to yesterday's US-British closing. It continued to fall 〇625 in the first hour, and then rose one-two-five at 2 PM, to four yuan, nine corners, five points, 〇625.

British-French: The opening price was 74 francs 56, the same as yesterday's closing price. It rose one pound sterling in the first hour, and then there was no change. Until 2 PM, it rose three pounds sterling again, to 74 francs 60.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The opening price of the New York cotton market was quite stable today, hovering in yesterday's range. The weather report continues to be good.

British Cotton: The price of the Liverpool cotton market was slightly loose today. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 6.28, down pounds sterling.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to be sluggish this morning and lacked brilliance. Prices fell slightly due to good news from the US wheat market. At noon, the July futures price was five shillings and three pence halfpenny, down two-five from yesterday's close.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened lower by about half a cent due to the very good weather in the producing areas, the new wheat crop is about to be harvested, and the Liverpool telegram was low, and the Canadian situation was again uncertain. Shortly after the opening, prices trended upward, and coarse grains opened higher two-five due to the strong statistical position. Later, prices gradually loosened, falling below yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet this morning. At noon, the transaction price for July and September futures was six pence 〇25, the same as yesterday's price.

New York: The New York rubber market opened slightly loose. July futures were closed out, and they were absorbed when prices were slightly lower. The forward market was still stable, eight to ten pounds less than yesterday's closing price.

Securities

New York: New York securities had little activity today because President Roosevelt advocated passing the entire new tax procedure in this congressional session. After the opening, prices of various securities generally fell. Oil stocks and steel stocks were especially reactive. After an hour of suffering, the market turned. The Dow Jones 30 industrial stock average price was 119.38, down six point six pounds.

The Headquarters Establishes a General Anti-Opium Association in Wuchang, Appointing Enthusiastic and Impartial Individuals as Members, and Promulgates Organizational Regulations for National Awareness 102

Hankou Correspondence: The Chairman's Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission, in order to eradicate opium, has formulated "Implementation Measures for Opium Suppression," ordering the provincial and municipal governments of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Hunan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, Beiping, and Tianjin to comply with the measures to completely ban opium within six years. Article 9 of the measures stipulates that the implementing agencies should establish anti-opium committees in provinces or cities and anti-opium sub-committees in counties, with each level being responsible. In Wuchang, where the headquarters is located, a general anti-opium committee will be established to oversee everything. Now, the "Organizational Regulations of the General Anti-Opium Committee of the Headquarters" consisting of fourteen articles have been formulated and issued to the provincial and municipal governments of the country and the anti-opium supervisory offices for their information. These regulations are as follows: Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 9 of the Implementation Measures for Opium Suppression. Article 2: The association will have several members, appointed from enthusiastic and impartial anti-opium individuals from various provinces. They will not receive salaries, only travel expenses. Article 3: The association will designate three members as standing committee members and designate the director and deputy director of the Seventh Division of the headquarters as ex-officio members. Article 4: All matters that should be handled by the provincial and municipal governments and the provincial and municipal anti-opium committees, including the prohibition of planting and smoking opium, as well as rewards and punishments, will be supervised and assessed by the association in accordance with the provisions of the Implementation Measures. Article 5: All members may make suggestions on the promotion of the prohibition of planting and smoking opium and all matters related to opium suppression, and submit them in writing for discussion at meetings. Article 6: The association will hold a standing meeting once a week, but meetings may be convened temporarily for important matters. The approval of proposals will be decided by a majority vote of the members present. Article 7: All proposals approved by vote should be submitted to the chairman for consideration and implementation. Article 8: In order to accelerate the efficiency of the prohibition of planting and smoking opium in various provinces and cities, the association may, at any time, request the chairman to send personnel to carry out supervisory matters. Article 9: The supervisory opium suppression members sent to various provinces and cities may handle matters by order of the provincial or municipal government in conjunction with the chairman or mayor of the relevant jurisdiction. The members may also co-sign documents. Article 10: The association will establish a secretariat to be responsible for the following: drafting of documents, editing of proposals, recording of meetings, and propaganda on the prohibition of planting and smoking opium. Article 11: The association will have one chief secretary, two to four secretaries, several inspectors, four to six clerks, and four scribes. In addition to those assigned, personnel from the Seventh Division of the headquarters handling opium suppression may also serve concurrently without additional salary. Article 12: Detailed rules for the association's operations will be formulated separately. Article 13: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not fully covered. Article 14: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval. (24th)

Amidst Commercial Decline, the Hankou Market Presents a Depressing Scene; the Largest Cotton Mill and Money Exchange Announce Closure One After Another; Labor Disputes and Debt Litigation Cases are Extremely Numerous 103

Hankou Correspondence: The details of the decline of commerce in Hankou due to natural disasters, banditry, and the impact of rural bankruptcy have already been described in a previous letter. However, the depressing scene in the market and the recent problems that have occurred have become more profound and serious in a short period of time. The only department store, Huaxing Company, suddenly announced its closure due to excessive losses. The Cantonese shareholders are unable to provide assistance, and there is no hope of resuming business. The China Steel Products Trading Company, which was also a powerful enterprise in Hankou, also went bankrupt last week with a debt of 450,000 yuan due to financial difficulties. Unfortunately, two extremely serious problems occurred simultaneously on the evening of the 22nd. One was the complete early shutdown of the First Cotton Mill, and the other was the sudden collapse of Yuyuan Silver Exchange, a major player in the money industry. The First Cotton Mill has been operated by the foreign creditor Arnhold Brothers & Co. for five years. Due to the high cost of cotton and poor sales of yarn, it has been losing approximately 70,000 to 80,000 yuan per month, with accumulated losses of more than 4 million yuan. The shareholders of the mill are unable to invest more capital, and the preparations for the shutdown have been going on for several months. The final decision was made to shut down early on July 1st, leaving more than 500 workers unemployed. On the 23rd, all the employees sent representatives to request six months of severance pay. The manager, Song Lifeng, and the deputy manager, Li Gongjian, convened an emergency meeting of all shareholders on the 24th to discuss this matter, but no results have been achieved. Yuyuan Silver Exchange, located on Poyang Street in the Third Special District, has been the leader of the money industry in Hankou. On the evening of the 22nd, it had to close down due to financial difficulties. Its debts amounted to 2.2 million yuan. The manager, Wang Huiqing, and the deputy manager, Shi Sicheng, left Hankou one after another and entrusted lawyer Chen Zhuo and accountant Xie Lin to liquidate the debts on their behalf. The silver exchange's head office is located in Shanghai, and it has absorbed a large amount of deposits in Hankou. Its closure has had a huge impact on the financial community in Hankou. In addition, the decline of various industries is a widespread phenomenon. For example, the Jijishui Electric Company's income from water and electricity in May decreased by 40,000 to 50,000 yuan compared to the same month last year. The situation is even worse for those with weak capital. Furthermore, city government and court cases involving labor disputes and debt litigation are numerous. These serious problems cannot be solved in a short period of time. Currently, there are continuous heavy rains and the river is rising rapidly. The villagers are hoping for rain, but it has turned into bitter rain. If another flood unfortunately occurs, it is unknown what the situation will be like. (24th)

Stabilizing Finances in Beiping; The City Government Discusses Preventive Measures with the Banking Community; Various Banks Form a Joint Treasury for Mutual Support 104

Beiping Correspondence: Since the collapse of the Minghua Bank in Beiping, the Jushengyuan Silver Exchange followed suit due to financial difficulties. As of the 22nd, the financial turmoil has affected the Tonghexiang and Zhengyang Silver Exchanges, leading to widespread rumors and creating a serious situation. To stabilize public confidence and the financial market, the city government convened a meeting at 10 a.m. on the 21st, inviting the managers of over ten banks, including the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Continental Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Yien Yieh Bank, and China South Bank, to discuss measures to prevent the turmoil. It was decided that the city government, the Chamber of Commerce, the Banking Association, and the Silver Money Industry Association would each nominate a representative to negotiate specific measures. The first meeting was held at 10 a.m. on the 22nd. Additionally, at 3 p.m. on the 11th, the city government summoned Zou Quansun, chairman of the City Chamber of Commerce, Leng Jiaheng, committee member, Cai Yuan, director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Cheng Fan, director of the Finance Bureau, and Yu Jin, director of the Public Security Bureau, to discuss proper measures to maintain the silver exchanges. The following resolutions were made: (1) No silver exchange shall arbitrarily suspend or close business in the future. If any financial difficulties arise, the shareholders shall bear unlimited liability in accordance with the law and be subject to supervision by city government officials. (2) Fixed-term depositors in the silver exchanges shall not be allowed to discount and withdraw their deposits early. Ordinary depositors should also endure the difficulties together, mutually supporting each other and refraining from withdrawing large amounts of cash without reason, so as not to affect the financial market. These measures will be communicated to all members by the Chamber of Commerce and the Silver Money Industry Association, and the city government will also order the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus to supervise them at all times. Any violations will be treated as disrupting the financial market.

Regarding the financial turmoil, according to Mayor Yuan Liang, the recent closure of the Jushengyuan and Tonghexiang Silver Exchanges was exploited by malicious individuals to spread rumors. The closure of these silver exchanges was due to their own internal problems, and it does not have any significant impact on other banks or the city market. The city government has ordered the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus to investigate and order the two silver exchanges to be liquidated within two weeks. Furthermore, regarding the financial situation in Beiping, the city government has discussed stabilization and maintenance measures with the Beiping banking community and the City Chamber of Commerce, and it has been decided that there will be no further bank failures. The city government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to arrest anyone who fabricates rumors and attempts to create a panic, and to punish them for disrupting the financial market. The financial situation in the city should stabilize in the shortest possible time. To apprehend those who fabricate rumors and disrupt the financial market, the city government issued a special proclamation on the 21st stating: "Since this city's financial market has been stable for many years, the recent closure of the Jushengyuan Silver Exchange is solely due to its own problems and has no significant impact on other banks or the city market. The city government is investigating and ordering the exchange to be liquidated as quickly as possible. However, some ignorant individuals have taken the opportunity to spread rumors and cause alarm among the public. Some depositors in the silver exchanges have not investigated and have been alarmed, spreading false information and rushing to withdraw their deposits. It should be understood that the city's financial market is very stable. Such self-inflicted disturbances will not only harm both parties but will also affect the market. In addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau to conduct thorough investigation and suppression, anyone who fabricates rumors and attempts to incite others will be arrested immediately and punished to the fullest extent of the law. This proclamation is issued to be strictly observed."

Just as the city government was making efforts to quell the financial turmoil, a run on the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank occurred on the morning of the 22nd. The bank was well-prepared and allowed unlimited cash withdrawals. The various banks in Beiping also assisted in accepting and redeeming the bank's notes. The bank's business hours were extended by one hour on that day. Normal procedures were followed on the 23rd, a Sunday. Therefore, the number of those making withdrawals had decreased by 3 p.m. on the 22nd. Since the Public Security Bureau was ordered by the city government to arrest those who fabricated rumors and attempted to incite others, it began to make arrests on the 23rd. In one day, a total of fifteen people who refused to accept China Agricultural and Industrial Bank notes were arrested. They are currently under interrogation and will be charged with disrupting the financial market.

To stabilize the market, the various silver exchanges in Beiping have now united and formed a joint treasury, mutually supporting each other and bearing joint responsibility to avoid financial difficulties. At the first meeting to rescue the market, held at the city government at 11 a.m. on the 22nd, Mayor Yuan Liang attended and gave instructions. The meeting resulted in a decision that the Silver Money Industry Association would mortgage a four million yuan loan note to the Banking Association for two million yuan in cash to assist in circulation. At 9 a.m. on the same morning, the Chamber of Commerce held an emergency meeting, inviting representatives from various merchants to attend. Chairman Zou Quansun delivered a speech, hoping that all members would consider the overall situation and work together under the principles established by the city government to maintain the financial market, so as not to allow the Beiping financial market to collapse further. Based on the above situation, it is hoped that the financial turmoil in Beiping will be quelled in a very short period of time. (22nd)

Overseas Chinese in Vietnam Eagerly Hope to Improve the Sino-Vietnamese Trade Treaty—Presenting Eight Points to the Government 105

Shantou Correspondence: The Pacific liner from Saigon arrived in Shantou yesterday, carrying a large number of unemployed overseas Chinese returning home. According to one of them, there used to be over 300,000 overseas Chinese engaged in trade in Vietnam. However, due to the decline of industry and commerce in recent years, the number has decreased by about 100,000. Therefore, unemployed overseas Chinese are continuously returning home, and the cargo transportation business in Southeast Asia is also shrinking. This is truly regrettable. Before the expiration of the old treaty in 1929, Vietnamese goods imported into China, such as rice, timber, etc., were worth about 50 to 60 million yuan, while Chinese goods imported into Vietnam were worth about 10 million yuan. After the expiration of the old treaty, the Vietnamese authorities treated Chinese goods as goods from countries without treaties, levying taxes at rates that were increased by more than twenty times. For example, Chinese silk fabrics, paper, porcelain, tea, fruits, and other goods were subjected to heavy taxes, causing the total value of exports to Vietnam to drop from 50 to 60 million yuan per year to 3 to 4 million yuan, falling to one-twentieth of the original amount. Currently, the Shantou Nanyang Business Association is continuing to regulate and allocate shipments before a new Sino-Vietnamese treaty is officially concluded, in order to avoid excessive losses. At the same time, Vietnamese goods sold in China are affected due to the common economic contraction. Therefore, merchants and residents of Guangdong and overseas Chinese in Vietnam believe that the signing of the appendices to the Sino-Vietnamese trade treaty is crucial to the prosperity or decline of their industries and commerce in the future. Therefore, the overseas Chinese have listed eight items and requested the government to improve them when concluding the treaty: (1) Improve the new regulations for Chinese immigrants. Any inhumane practices should be abolished in the spirit of Sino-French friendship, such as fingerprinting at the immigration office, having people enter iron sheds, and moving luggage through clothing inspection booths. (2) Reduce taxes on Chinese goods entering Vietnam. Transit taxes should be levied according to the Siberian-European cargo transit methods for goods transferred from Haiphong to Yunnan and Guangxi, and should not be subject to transit taxes. (3) Reduce the burden on overseas Chinese residents. The annual residence tax (head tax) should be kept to a minimum, at least at the same level as in Singapore and Thailand. (4) Since China governs the country by party, Vietnamese officials should not send detectives to monitor the actions of overseas Chinese party members or their meetings, and party-state documents should not be arbitrarily inspected or confiscated. (5) Do not excessively interfere with the education of overseas Chinese. Restrictions on the curriculum and the required number of hours for French language courses should be lifted. The teaching of party doctrine and the strict selection of teachers should not be exempted. (6) The inspection of local Chinese newspapers is limited to submitting manuscripts at noon every day, resulting in many important news items being missed. New items unrelated to local laws are often arbitrarily removed, and there are no standard restrictions on the entry of domestic newspapers and magazines. (7) Do not abuse exit orders by arbitrarily ordering the departure of intellectuals deemed to be extremist elements. There should be certain restrictions in the future. (8) If the children of overseas Chinese students want to return to China, they must find a shop to guarantee that they will return to Vietnam within a specified period. If they die in China, a report must be made to the Vietnamese consulate for verification. Overseas Chinese in Vietnam request that the central government negotiate with the French side to improve the above items.

Songjiang: River Police Inspector Seizes Native Opium Trafficker 106

Diao Yushan, patrolman No. 6 of the second detachment of the first district of the Water Police Team, was patrolling the vicinity of the Xindongmen bus station today when he noticed a suspicious person among the disembarking passengers. He immediately went forward to question him. The passenger looked flustered and spoke hesitantly, which made him even more suspicious. He searched him and found twenty taels of Yunnan opium and thirty taels of Sichuan opium, a total of fifty taels, marked with a lion symbol. He took him back to the detachment for interrogation. The man confessed that his name was Jin Yuqi, from Hebei, 40 years old, living at No. 15 Daxing Street, Shanghai, and that he was a vegetable seller. He said that a friend named Zhang had bought the opium and asked him to carry it, and that Zhang would receive it at the station and pay him five yuan. Based on the confession, Detachment Leader Hu immediately submitted the case to the Third Brigade Headquarters for investigation.

The Cai Fan Industry Association in our town, in order to abolish exorbitant taxes in Jiangsu Province, presented a petition to Mr. Han Guojun, chairman of the Jiangsu Province Donation and Tax Supervision Committee, yesterday, requesting the abolition of the redundant banquet tax, and requesting the provincial government to issue an order to stop the tax, in order to alleviate the difficulties of merchants.

Changzhou: Yu Min Cloth Factory Female Worker Commits Suicide 110

Shi Heying, a 21-year-old female worker at the Yumin Weaving Factory outside the East Gate of Wuyi, who was from the Shijia Village near the factory, was working the night shift at the factory when, on the late night of the 23rd, she took advantage of a moment of unguardedness and hanged herself by the stairs in the front of the factory. The factory immediately sent someone to notify her family and reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau for relay to the County Court for examination. Prosecutor Guan Junjie went to examine the body on the 24th and confirmed that she had died by hanging. The body was prepared by her family in a coffin and collected. As for the reason for the female worker's suicide, it is said to be due to unhappy marriage. It is said that the deceased had been betrothed to someone by her parents, but the marriage was called off because she was not liked by her in-laws, and she returned to her parents' home. Recently, her parents arranged for her to marry someone named Bai, and the wedding was approaching. The female worker, saddened by the pain of being a child bride and the unhappiness of marriage, developed a world-weary attitude.

Jiangyin: Verdict in the Case of Destroying the Public Security Bureau 111

Li Zongyao, Director of the First Branch of the Beiguan Public Security Bureau, had a conflict with the Fire Brigade on May 19th. Ignorant troublemakers destroyed the interior of the Public Security Bureau. The county government successively apprehended five suspects in this case: Liu Hancai, Gao Baosheng, Shen Bingzhi, Zhang Huinong, and Xing Shudong. Wang Peiqing and Shen Shigeng are at large. The provincial government ordered the case to be transferred to the judiciary. After investigation and interrogation by Judge Zhou Cheng, and with the testimony of officers such as Shi Hayulong from the branch bureau, a public trial concluded on the 22nd, and the verdict was pronounced on the 24th. The main text is as follows: Gao Baosheng, Shen Bingzhi, Liu Hancai, and Zhang Huinong are each sentenced to four years of imprisonment for jointly and publicly gathering a crowd on the scene to commit acts of violence and coercion. They are also each sentenced to four years of imprisonment for jointly destroying official documents in the custody of public officials, rendering them unusable. Each defendant's combined sentence is set at seven years. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Xing Shuxun is found not guilty. The trial proceedings against Wang Peiqing and Shen Baogen are suspended, and a warrant will be issued to the Higher Court for their arrest and subsequent interrogation. The related civil lawsuit is transferred to the civil court for trial. After the verdict, Gao Baosheng and others declared their dissatisfaction and stated their intention to appeal, and were subsequently taken back into custody.

Xiaoshan: 30,000 Mu of Sandbank Collapses in Xiaosibu 114

Xiaosibu, located in the Toupeng Township of eastern Xiaoshan, faces Haining County across the river and is densely populated. The original sandbank along the riverfront was approximately 30,000 mu. In recent years, the river's course has changed dramatically, and the intensity of the tides is unprecedented. Consequently, the riverbank has collapsed rapidly, and the entire 30,000 mu of mature sandbank has been submerged. Many residents have been forced to relocate. Recently, the riverbank collapse in that area has become severe and extremely dangerous. The base of the Gao Zhengxing Public Office and a small number of street foundations have already fallen into the water. Residents are dismantling their homes in a rush, and some are even unable to relocate in time. Impoverished farmers who are suffering from the riverbank collapse are displaced and destitute. Their cries of misery fill the air, a truly unbearable sight. It is hoped that the authorities will find a way to provide relief.

Director Huang Boqiao of Two Railway Bureaus Returned to China Yesterday - His Investigation of Railway Industries in Various Countries Was Very Thorough - A Chronic Illness Was Completely Cured After Treatment in Austria 116

Huang Boqiao, Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, returned to Shanghai yesterday aboard the Norddeutscher Lloyd ship "Scharnhorst" after being ordered by the Ministry of Railways to investigate railway industries in Europe and America and seeking treatment from famous doctors in Austria for his chronic illness. Many of his relatives, friends, and subordinates went to welcome him. Details are recorded as follows:

Returning by Ship

Director Huang departed from Shanghai on August 21st of last year to conduct his investigation. He first traveled east to Japan, stayed for about a week, and then took a ship to Canada and the United States. He then crossed the Atlantic Ocean to Europe, visiting countries such as England, Germany, France, Belgium, Austria, the Czech Republic, and Switzerland. He investigated the railway industries of various countries along the way in great detail, paying particular attention to the railway industries of England and Germany, where he stayed for a longer period. The British government and public also paid close attention to Huang's visit to England. Now, having completed his investigation, he returned to China aboard the "Scharnhorst."

Welcoming Relatives and Friends

The "Scharnhorst," carrying Director Huang, arrived in port at 8:00 AM yesterday. Among those who came to welcome him were Li Muyuan, Director of the Procurement Committee of the Ministry of Railways; Li Dachao, representative of Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau; and senior officials from the Railway Bureau, including Xu Yuanfang, Mo Heng, Xiao Weiguo, Liu Dingxin, Pu Dengqing, Hu Jicong, Cao Shengzhi, Ma Shaoping, Wang Bi, Wu Xihan, as well as Huang's relatives and friends, totaling more than thirty people.

Arrival in Shanghai

The "Scharnhorst" arrived at the Songkou port around 6:00 PM yesterday and docked at the Gongxiang Wharf at around 8:00 PM. When the ship docked, the ship's band played music in celebration. The welcoming party immediately boarded the ship. Director Huang, dressed in a white long gown, appeared refined and greeted the welcoming party in the guest room, shaking hands and chatting with them. He then told reporters that the investigation had been lengthy and that he would discuss the details with them at a later date. After speaking, he accompanied his wife to return to their residence to rest.

Chronic Illness Completely Cured

Before going abroad, Director Huang suffered from chronic diabetes, which recurred several times, causing soreness in both arms and threatening blindness in one eye. Although he had taken leave to seek treatment in Moganshan, he had not fully recovered. During this trip to Europe, he sought treatment from famous doctors in Austria, and his chronic illness has been cured. Director Huang used to wear black glasses to avoid bright light, but now he wears white crystal glasses, indicating a return to normalcy. His spirit is also very vigorous.

Arriving at the Bureau This Morning

Director Huang will arrive at the bureau this morning to resume his duties. He will also draft a report on the course of his investigation and will travel to Beijing within a few days to report everything to the Minister of Railways in person. Colleagues at the two railway bureaus are scheduled to hold a dinner party at the New Asia Hotel at noon on the 29th to welcome Director Huang.

Xin Xin News Agency reported that Feng Zhizheng, our country's Consul General in Amsterdam, Netherlands, returned to China on leave, accompanied by his wife, sons, and daughters, aboard the Norddeutscher Lloyd ship "Scharnhorst" which arrived in Shanghai at 8:00 PM last night. In the past, there were more than 3,000 overseas Chinese, but in recent years, the number has gradually decreased, and now there are only about 1,000 left. The Dutch government treats our overseas Chinese fairly well. However, there are indeed cases of harsh treatment of our compatriots in the Dutch East Indies. The embassy in the Netherlands has repeatedly received reports and has protested to the Dutch government several times, and the authorities have promised to improve the situation. Because the Dutch government's policies differ between its domestic territories and overseas colonies, the Dutch East Indies discriminates against Chinese, while the Netherlands itself treats overseas Chinese relatively well. After resting in Shanghai for one or two days, I will go to Beijing to report everything to the authorities. In the future, I plan to remain in the Ministry and await further assignment.

Commercial and Industrial Loans Will Be Implemented Soon - Expected to Begin Lending Before July 5th - The Loan Committee Has Drafted Loan Collateral - Mortgage Credit and Two Types of Lending Will Be Held Simultaneously 119

Xin Xin News Agency reports that the Shanghai Commercial and Industrial Loan Committee's regulations for guaranteeing loan recipients, organizational charters, procedures, detailed rules for guaranteeing loans, etc., have all been approved at the third meeting. Chairman Cai Zengji has prepared a document and submitted it to the Ministry of Finance for approval and promulgation. The office set up by the association on the second floor of the National Goods Bank has been prepared and is scheduled to open before July 5th. A reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency learned of the situation from banking circles yesterday, and details are recorded as follows:

Opening on July 5th

The office set up by the Commercial and Industrial Loan Committee on the second floor of the National Goods Bank has been prepared. The association's telephone number will be the same as the National Goods Bank's number, but a separate extension will be installed for contact. Staff will also be assigned. Currently, preparations are underway to invite several experts to provide guidance on improving technology in various factories and correcting the business direction of commercial firms after the loans are released. The association is scheduled to open before July 5th to accept loan applications from commercial and industrial firms. The 1st and 2nd of July are bank holidays.

Designated Banks and Money Shops to Lend

This loan will be divided into two types: mortgage loans and credit loans. Mortgage loans will be limited to 15 million, and credit loans will be limited to 5 million. The association will designate banks and money shops to lend. All factories manufacturing national goods, commercial firms selling national goods, and those transporting national goods for export are eligible to apply for loans. The collateral of various factories and commercial firms will be the first guarantee, and national treasury certificates will be the second guarantee. The association may send personnel at any time to supervise and inspect the use of loans by various factories and commercial firms to prevent them from being diverted for other purposes.

Specified Types of Loan Collateral

According to inquiries by reporters from the Xin Xin News Agency, factories or commercial firms applying for loans must submit commodities, machinery, valuable securities, and other collateral. However, (1) commodities must be easily salable, not easily perishable, insured by reputable firms, and stored in warehouses; (2) machinery, regardless of the type, must be the latest model with fast manufacturing capacity and speed; (3) securities must be government bonds or other valuable stocks issued by the central and local governments.

Two Repayment Deadlines are Set

The market price or valuation of collateral for mortgage loans must be determined by experts. For credit loans, only two reputable commercial firms need to provide joint and several guarantees. However, the total amount requested may not exceed half of the capital and public reserve of each factory or commercial firm. The monthly interest rate for both mortgage and credit loans may not exceed eight percent. If a factory or commercial firm cannot afford the full monthly interest, the lending banks and money shops may apply to the loan association to submit it to the Ministry of Finance for approval and subsidy of two percent monthly interest. The repayment period for mortgage loans is one year, and the repayment period for credit loans can follow the usual practice of repayment at the end of each closing period. Post Office Launches Transfer Telegraphic Money Order 124

Shanghai Postal Administration Savings and Remittance Notice No. 45 states that in order to make public remittances faster, each post office in this district has now launched transfer telegraphic money orders. The procedures are as follows: (1) The initial transfer of the telegraphic money order is to use an ordinary money order, stamp it with the words "Transfer Telegraphic Money Order," and hand it over to the remitter, who will mail the money order by registered mail to the telegraphic money order transfer office for verification, without needing to prepare a separate letter. If the payment office has direct telegraphic transfer facilities, the transfer office will directly telegraph the money to the payment office. If the payment office does not have direct telegraphic transfer facilities, it will be transferred by mail through the nearest telegraphic money order transfer office to the payment office. However, the public should note that remitting money using a transfer telegraphic money order is only effective under certain circumstances, such as when the payment office is far away from the remitting office. If an ordinary money order is faster according to the situation, the post office should temporarily notify the remitter. (2) In addition to collecting ordinary money order fees, if a reply is required, a reply fee should be charged. An additional telegraphic transfer fee of 25 cents and a telegraph fee of 60 cents per telegraphic money order should also be charged. If the telegraph exceeds 20 words, an additional 5 cents per word should be charged for the excess words. (3) To expedite the payment of the transfer telegraphic money order, the remitter should clearly state the name and address of the payee in detail. (4) After the remitter has paid the remittance and the various fees mentioned in Section 2 above, they should properly keep the receipt issued by the post office (the second copy of the money order application form with the added word). This receipt should be presented for any subsequent inquiries about the money order. (5) If the payee of the transfer telegraphic money order cannot prove that they are the payee, the money order should be paid with a guarantor. (6) For other details, please inquire at the money order office of each post office. This is hereby announced for general information.

Strong Winds and Rain in Zhenjiang Damaged China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Ships - The Li Hang, Mao Li, and Kuai Li Ships Suffered Extremely Heavy Damage 125

Zhenjiang has been hit by three major storms in a row. This Sunday, a sudden gale rose, accompanied by heavy rain. From morning till night, the storms did not cease. Countless civilian boats and barges along the Zhenjiang riverbank were hit and damaged by the violent winds and rain. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Zhenjiang branch had just been taken over by Director Xin Yaoxiang of the inland river shipping Zhenjiang branch, and the ships were docked at the river wharf. However, before the ships were assigned to any schedules, they were damaged by the waves in the river, causing considerable damage.

Three Ships Damaged in a Row. The Li Hang, which runs the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou line, was anchored on the riverbank when it was battered by the heavy storm. The hull suffered major damage. Two or three zhang of the ship's port side was smashed, and the wooden rail at the stern was completely destroyed by the raging waves. The extent of the damage is difficult to describe. In addition, the Mao Li and Kuai Li were struck by the wind and waves, and the railings on both sides of the two ships were completely destroyed. One of the large wooden beams was broken by the huge waves, and the hulls of both ships were also damaged and flooded. All three ships are unusable.

Request for Inspection and Repair. Yesterday, Xin Yaoxiang, director of the Zhenjiang branch, sent a detailed report to the Shanghai General Office after inspecting and verifying the damage to the ships, requesting the Shanghai General Office to send engineers to Zhenjiang as soon as possible to inspect the damage so that they can be repaired and officially put into service on the inland river routes. Xin also stated that inland river ships are usually repaired in Jiangyin, but the three ships are so badly damaged that they cannot be sailed to Jiangyin and can only be inspected and repaired in Zhenjiang. Yesterday, the head office was discussing sending staff to Zhenjiang to inspect and estimate the repairs.

He was arrested as a secret worker under the strange Westerner, and it was by no means as the Japanese newspapers claimed that he was arrested for relying on someone who had dealings with the Japanese or the so-called Blue Shirts Society, which is completely unfounded. After the case was solved, it was discovered that Yuan Shu had many aliases, such as Yuan Xueyi, Yuan Xiaotao, Rong Jun, Li Huimin, etc., all of which were used by Yuan Shu. It was only after the strange Westerner's case was solved that his conspiracy was discovered. Currently, Yuan Shu and the strange Westerner have been sent to the competent court for joint handling of the case.

National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Cables Ministry of Finance, Requesting Return of Confiscated Treasury Silver 129

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: "Respectfully addressed to the Ministry of Finance, Nanjing. We have recently received a jointly sealed letter from Song Pinting, manager of the Deshengyong Silver Shop in Shanhaiguan, and 105 other firms, including Yongyuhang. The letter states that merchants have traditionally operated the Deshengyong Silver Shop in Qitiaohutong in Shanhaiguan city, with branch offices in Nanguan outside the city, engaging in financial remittance and exchange, as well as buying and selling remittance drafts. Historically, because the main and branch offices are located inside and outside the city walls, the branch offices outside the city often collect and store remittance funds. To ensure safety, they are transported to the main office inside the city for storage, ready for remittance procedures if needed. Every day, special delivery personnel carry public receipts, i.e., return receipts, for delivery purposes. The funds are stored in nature, so they are not recorded in any accounts. Usually, there are hired workers specifically for delivering scattered cash payments within the street. However, carrying cash and banknotes on the road is most easily targeted by bandits, creating a risk of robbery. Therefore, merchants traditionally prepare vests, commonly known as 'silver bags,' with two pockets on the left and right sides, specifically for the cash delivery personnel to wear, so that they can carry cash discreetly, thus slowing down the pirates' plan to steal the sea. This kind of vest is a common custom for merchants, and it has been around for a long time. (Omitted middle section). Unexpectedly, on the 24th of last month, the Qinhuangdao Shanhaiguan branch card dispatched many people to search the main office and confiscated 12,675 yuan of silver in the vault, as well as silver bags and remittance slips, falsely accusing them of smuggling. The staff members Song Zun and Chen Jinsheng were detained by the local Public Security Bureau. Although 105 reputable merchants in the area jointly testified that it was not smuggling, the negotiations were ineffective. The branch card arbitrarily searched and confiscated the treasury silver, falsely accusing it of smuggling. We do not know where the 'private' comes from or where the 'transport' begins. As for the silver bags worn by the silver delivery personnel, they are used for concealing cash deliveries within the street to prevent bandits from coveting them. This kind of custom is also common among silver shops and cash delivery personnel. According to our knowledge, although the use of silver bags has decreased since the establishment of the bank clearing house in Shanghai, they are still used occasionally. They cannot be regarded as evidence of smuggling. Furthermore, the silver delivery slips are clear receipts for the arrival of silver and can be traced back to the original root, which is sufficient to prove it. May we ask, every silver shop in Shanghai stores hundreds of thousands of cash, which is not a small amount. And every shop also has silver bags for silver delivery personnel and silver delivery slips. According to this logic, could this also be considered evidence of smuggling? How can this be reasonable? Most of the silver confiscated from the shop was entrusted by various customers for remittance and exchange of goods in Tianjin. There are also ticket stubs that can be checked. However, when the Tianjin remitting party heard the news of the confiscation, they rushed to the market to exchange the drafts, hindering financial transactions and causing great panic. In order to clarify the facts, we respectfully request your association to forward our request to return the confiscated silver to maintain financial stability. Therefore, we jointly send this telegram to your ministry for review. We implore you to consider the suffering of the merchants and promptly order the Qinhuangdao Customs to correct this overstepping action and return all the confiscated treasury silver to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Respectfully and urgently. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, with seal."

The Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Promotion Association held its first staff meeting yesterday at 2 p.m. at its headquarters. Attendees included [names omitted], presided over by [name omitted], with [name omitted] as secretary. The meeting proceeded as follows: First, the chairman reported on the association's mission, followed by discussion of proposals. (1) Regarding the submission of attendance reports by various schools as soon as possible for statistical purposes (decision): a. Schools already in session should submit their attendance reports within three days. b. Group attendance reports should be submitted to the respective group leaders on the day after attendance for daily dissemination of information. c. A simplified form should be filled out first, followed by a detailed form after inspection. (2) How to urge the establishment of schools that have not yet been established (decision): a. Schools run independently that have reported preparations but have not yet opened should be ordered to open before July 1st. b. Substitute teachers who have not yet submitted their registration lists should be notified to contact us before the 8th of this month. If they fail to do so by the deadline, it will be considered a waiver, and alternates will be assigned. (3) How to deal with party branches and groups that do not comply with the order to establish schools (decision): a. After identifying groups that have not reported the establishment of schools, the group leaders will be responsible for investigating them and reporting back before July 10th. b. (4) How to divide the work of inspection (decision): a. In addition to the original attendees being responsible for the inspection, additional personnel should be assigned for spot checks. b. Each inspector should be responsible for twenty schools, and each school should be inspected once a month. The main point is to check the number of students. (5) How to prevent students from dropping out voluntarily (decision): a. In the Chinese area, the principals should report to the nearest police station to enforce attendance. In the concession, they should be persuaded. b. The completion of children's education should be included in compulsory education management. The meeting adjourned at 10 a.m.

Shaanxi Province Construction Loan: Banks in this City Refuse to Accept; Using Land as Mortgage is Inconsistent with Regulations; Banks Negotiate and Send Letters to Branches Rejecting Politely 132

According to the Dagong News Agency, Shao Lizhi, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, believes that Shaanxi's construction projects urgently need to be promoted, but the provincial treasury is empty and the economy is in difficulty. The Construction Department and the Municipal Construction Committee of the Provincial Government took the lead in contacting the Xi'an branches of Chinese, Communications, Jin City, Shanghai, Zhejiang Industrial and other banks, intending to use land as collateral and the central government's monthly construction funds as guarantee to sign a construction loan of 300,000 yuan with the banks. After several contacts, each branch signed a letter of opinion and submitted it to the Shanghai head office for instructions. According to banking news yesterday, the banking community should assist Shaanxi authorities in borrowing construction loans, as it is related to the municipal construction of Xijing. However, the proposed mortgage and guarantee are improper and cannot be accepted according to regulations. Therefore, after consultation with the authorities, it was decided to politely reject it. The original letter is recorded as follows: "Respectfully informing you, we previously received a letter reporting that the Xi'an Municipal Construction Committee intends to mortgage the land in the new urban area to the banking group for a loan of 300,000 yuan, requesting your instructions, and a copy of the letter and mortgage overdraft loan agreement from the committee has been received and reviewed. As the construction of roads in Xijing is related to municipal construction, we should all assist. However, the use of land as a mortgage cannot be accepted according to regulations. Furthermore, it is inappropriate to designate the central government's monthly construction funds as a guarantee. There are many obstacles in the negotiation. Therefore, we are writing to you specifically, hoping that you will politely reject it. Sincerely, China, Communications, Jin City, Shanghai, Zhejiang Industrial, all head offices."

Chinese Merchants' Company Feeds Electricity to Songjiang: Laying Transmission Lines Between Shanghai and Songjiang 137

The contract and other documents have been signed and submitted to the Public Utilities Bureau for review. It is expected that power transmission between the two parties can be implemented in early August. According to the Dagong News Agency, the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company is responding to the request of the Songjiang Power Plant, and the two parties will implement joint power feeding. The contract and draft electricity tariff have been determined, and the laying of transmission lines will begin next month. The details are recorded as follows:

Contract Signed

The Songjiang Power Plant is a business jointly funded by merchants. The internal scale is not large. Nowadays, the residents of the county and townships have gradually become dense. In addition to the increased electricity consumption of shops and households in the urban area, electricity is also supplied to various oil mills and water pumping factories to power machinery. Therefore, the power supply is sometimes insufficient. For this reason, the company has specially contacted the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company in this city to feed electricity for relief. At present, both parties have signed the draft contract and electricity tariff. After the approval of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, it can be implemented.

Laying Transmission Lines

The Shanghai-Songjiang power transmission line is currently being planned by the Electrical Engineering Department of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company. All the materials to be used have also been prepared. The main line starts from the South Railway Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road, passes through Longhua, Xin Longhua Xinzhuang, and to the Xinqiao section, which is laid by the Chinese Merchants. Starting from Songjiang West Station, passing through Mingxing Bridge to Sijing section, which is built by the Songjiang Power Plant, and a power transmission shed is set up in the middle of the main line, and the number of kilowatt-hours of electricity is recorded by the Chinese Merchants every day, and the accounts are settled once.

Power Feeding Date

According to Zhu Chongxian, director of the General Affairs Department of the Chinese Merchants' Electric Company yesterday, the current power of the company is only for the use of the whole city. This time, Songjiang requested power supply, originally to develop the electrical business in the inland counties and cities and to assist the needs of the rural areas, so we tried our best to contact them. The draft contract has been exchanged and amended by both parties and the laying of the pole line will be carried out next month. It is expected that the power will be turned on in early August.

Insufficient Lung Beds in the Isolation Hospital of the Public Works Bureau 139

The Health Committee of the Public Works Bureau, in view of the increase in the number of out-of-hospital lung patients, and the original lung beds in the Isolation Hospital of the Public Works Bureau are insufficient, specially instructed the Health Department to review whether the lung beds in the hospital can be increased. Now the director of the Health Department has written a report and submitted it to the committee. The report states that the hospital has previously received patients with lung disease who came to the hospital requesting accommodation because of their critical situation and could not refuse them, so they tried to make room for 10 beds specifically for accommodating lung patients. As a result, the hospital's beds are in short supply. When there is an emergency, it is found that it is insufficient to allocate. At present, those admitted to the hospital with lung disease are either in critical condition or severe cases with infectious risks and should not be accommodated together with those in the early stage or mild cases of lung disease. Therefore, the establishment of lung beds in other sanatoriums is not to reduce the burden of the hospital. Since there is no other appropriate place to accommodate them, the isolation hospital is limited by the insufficient number of beds, and the accommodation period for long-term lung disease patients has to be restricted. It is best to set a maximum accommodation period. Although this restriction does not necessarily have to be enforced, it will be beneficial for patients to be transferred to a suitable place. In terms of climate, those with lung disease generally find it more suitable to return to their hometown for rest than to be confined in the hospital. The Health Committee also advocates establishing a maximum accommodation period for lung patients in the Isolation Hospital of the Public Works Bureau. The lack of lung disease treatment facilities in the concession is recorded, and opportunities will be taken to consider it as soon as possible. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Bureau held a meeting yesterday and approved the minutes of the committee meeting and filed them.

North German Company's New Ship: First Voyage to the Far East Arrives in Shanghai; Total Height of the Ship Reaches Nine Floors, Unprecedented Speed; Excellent Facilities with Swimming Pool and Sports Ground 144

The giant express ship Scharnhorst, newly built by the North German Company of Germany, sailed from Bremen, Germany to the Far East on the 8th of last month and arrived in Shanghai at 8 p.m. yesterday and docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf. The ship is the best of all ships traveling to the Far East, and its speed is enough to break the records of previous years. The perfection of the ship's equipment is also unmatched by other ships. In addition to bedrooms, reception rooms, and dance halls, there are super-class kitchens, swimming pools, sports grounds, condensing rooms, and artificial air equipment. The ship is scheduled to receive visits from all walks of life starting the day after tomorrow, for a total of three days: 27th, 28th, and 29th. It is scheduled to return to Europe on July 1st. The details are recorded as follows:

Overall View of the Ship

The North German express new ship Scharnborst has a volume of 18,300 tons. It uses electricity for propulsion and burns gasoline instead of coal, so its speed is extremely fast. It can travel 21 nautical miles per hour. The ship has a total of nine floors from the bottom of the ship to the top. The ship can accommodate 142 first-class passengers, 144 second-class passengers, and six cargo holds, occupying a total of 14,000 cubic meters. When driven by electricity, it can generate 26,000 horsepower. The entire ship's exterior is white, and the hull is black. The highest floor is the engine room, followed by the swimming pool and sports field, then the bedrooms and reception rooms, then the first-class bedrooms and offices, and the lowest is the cargo hold. The voyage from Shanghai to Southern Europe, Italy, takes 23 days, which is 24 hours faster than the fastest Far East ship.

Features of the Ship

The characteristics of the ship are: 1. Propulsion by electricity; 2. The joints are not connected with iron nails, but with hot molten iron solidification, which can reduce weight and resist strong winds and waves. In addition, the entire ship is equipped with new-style air exchange equipment to keep the air fresh all day long. Therefore, the climate on the ship is mild. The food is preserved by condensing gas. The ship also has various general-purpose shops and barber shops. As for the bedrooms, dance halls, restaurants, etc., they are better than other ships.

Arrival Situation

At 8 p.m. yesterday, the ship entered the Huangpu River and slowly docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf, standing majestically. The torches in the cabin were brightly lit, as bright as day. After the ship arrived, the ship's music team played music to celebrate. Then, the luggage was loaded and unloaded. About one hundred passengers came to Shanghai last night, which was quite crowded. Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Railway Bureaus, and Liu Haisu, President of the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts, both came to Shanghai on the ship. The ship is scheduled to receive visits from all walks of life for two days starting tomorrow and is scheduled to return to Europe on the first day of next month.

According to Dagong News Agency, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Cigarette Industry Association held a business meeting at its clubhouse on May Bai Ge Road at 3 pm yesterday to discuss measures to ban handmade cigarettes and restore the operation of cigarette factories, and decided to recommend Mr. Wu Ting-sheng to visit the Finance Minister Kong to request relief. Details are as follows:

Yesterday's Meeting

The Shanghai Chinese Merchant Cigarette Industry Association held a business meeting yesterday afternoon. Both Roads Rectify Street Cleaning, Shanghai South and Zhabei Improve Garbage Disposal Methods 146

In order to rectify street cleaning, the Municipal Health Bureau is striving to improve the garbage bins originally placed on the streets. It was first tested in the area under the jurisdiction of the Wenmiao Police Station in the Shanghai South District, and achieved remarkable results. The bureau has jointly adopted the improved garbage disposal method in the Shanghai South and Zhabei districts with the Municipal Public Security Bureau. A few days ago, the Municipal Public Security Bureau ordered various district offices to work with the Shanghai South Health Office to send police to persuade residents, shops, and factories to prepare small garbage bins for indoor use, and all garbage should be dumped into the bins. At the same time, the Health Bureau removed all garbage bins on the streets and sent sanitation workers to ring the bell at each household in the early morning and around 2 pm every day. After hearing the bell, the households immediately dumped the garbage in the small garbage bins into the garbage truck pushed by the sanitation workers. Since the implementation of this improvement measure, the streets have been clean and tidy, and the residents have found it convenient. It will be promoted to the whole city in the future.

Fraudulent Sale of Human-Made Silk Pretending to be the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Finance, Falsely Entrusted to Sell Human-Made Silk to Carry out Fraud 149

Huang Shou-ren from Qingdong, who claimed to be the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Finance, is 36 years old and lives at No. 91 Yonghua Lane, North Sichuan Road. Recently, he colluded with Shen Xing-lu (27 years old, from Ningbo, living at No. 2 Baifu Lane, Broadway Road), Lin Ze-yuan (48 years old, from Hubei, living at No. 164 Chunyang Lane, Dong Youheng Road), and Le Xin-zhang (54 years old, from Ningbo, living at No. 5 Chengye Lane, Fuxu Road), falsely claiming that the Jianghai Customs Tax Department recently had 100 boxes of confiscated human-made silk for sale. They solicited business from Qiu Zi-feng (40 years old) from Wuxi, who lives at No. 7 Xigui Xing Lane, Wuwei Road, Public Concession, and is engaged in the silk business. The fraud was unsuccessful and was reported to the French Concession Police by Qiu. Detective Inspector Jiang Fu-tian, detective Cao Fu-chang, and detective Lu Lu-xian went to Zhengjia Muqiao Street

Dafang Hotel

In room 402, all the above-mentioned people were detained. A newly carved ivory seal and a wooden seal, as well as a newspaper about the customs auctioning human-made silk and a copy of the order form signed by both parties, were found in Huang Shou-ren's pocket. They were taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. First, Gu Shou-xi, the lawyer representing the police department, stated the case, saying that the defendant was arrested for the crime of fraud and extortion. The police station still needs to investigate in detail and requested a postponement of two weeks to detain the defendant for detailed investigation before

suing for trial. Then, Jiang Fu-tian, the detective in charge of the case at the police station, reported that the plaintiff was introduced by Li Guo-xian on June 10 and talked to Shen Xing-lu about the sale of 100 boxes of human-made silk that Jianghai Customs had confiscated on the Jinan Maru ship in August last year. On the 17th, Shen accompanied the plaintiff to the Central Bank to meet Huang Shou-ren, who claimed to be the Secretary-General of the Ministry of Finance. At that time, the price of each box was set at 250 yuan, and 15,000 yuan in cash must be paid first before delivery. An order was scheduled to be placed on the 21st. In fact, there was no such goods at all. The whole plan was designed to defraud. The plaintiff was afraid of being deceived, so he inquired with the Jianghai Customs Tax Department and learned that the goods had already been

advertised for auction, which was indeed a scam. It was also found that Huang Shou-ren was not the Secretary-General of the Ministry of Finance. Therefore, the Customs Anti-Smuggling Section reported to the Water Patrol Police, which was forwarded to the French Concession Police. On the one hand, the plaintiff was ordered to falsely invite Huang Shou-ren and others to open a room at the Dafang Hotel to place an order, with Shen Xing-lu acting as the frontman, Huang Shou-ren as the guarantor, and Lin and Le as witnesses. The detectives waited, and when they were about to pay the money after writing the receipt and order form, the detectives entered the room and arrested the defendants. The receipt, order form, and other evidence were presented to the court. In addition, the plaintiff Qiu Zi-feng filed a complaint about the previous situation, which was the same as what Inspector Jiang said. He also said that the merchant and his younger brother Yu Jia had been subjected to the same plan last year and had been defrauded of

tens of thousands of dollars. When these people came, they were all dressed in Western suits and were very generous. After being defrauded, they disappeared. This time, the merchant inquired with the provincial office and learned the details, etc. Huang Shou-ren confessed that he was a staff member in the Ministry of Finance, not the Secretary-General. This time, he was indeed deceived by others and hesitated. Shen Xing-lu confessed that he was introduced to Huang Shou-ren by Lin Ze-yuan and only knew that Huang was a first-class staff member of the Ministry of Finance. Li Guo-xian introduced the Qiu family to Huang Shou-ren and Lin Ze-yuan to sell customs goods and asked me to come forward to place an order. Lin Ze-yuan confessed that he had known Huang Shou-ren for many years and Shen Xing-lu for only a year. Huang said that in August last year, the customs had a Jinan Maru

confiscated 100 boxes of tax-evading human-made silk. After the detention, a Japanese named Oda asked Huang to intercede with the Tax Department and ordered a penalty. Because the Japanese was unable to pay the penalty, the goods were still in customs and were to be sold. Therefore, he introduced them. He did not know that there was no such goods. The remaining words were vague. Le Xin-zhang confessed that he was a tailor and that they had asked him to go to the Dafang Hotel to be a witness on the order form. He did not know about the fraud. The witness Li Guo-xian confessed that he was from Guangdong and was formerly the Deputy Manager of Shen Yu Xing. Shen Xing-lu came to ask if I had customs human-made silk to buy. Dang knew the situation. After Qiu Huan-ying pushed and brought the confession, the court ordered a postponement of the trial to 10 am on July 10. The defendants were remanded.

The Whole City's Pawn Industry Appeals to Shorten the Maturity Period of Pawned Goods Businesses are Closing Down One After Another Due to the Impact of Soaring Prices If We Do Not Save Them, the Whole Body Will Collapse in Less Than Two Years Presenting to the Social Bureau for Approval to Change the Maturity Period to One Year 150

According to Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Pawn Industry Association submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau yesterday, requesting to shorten the maturity period of pawned goods in order to provide relief. The original document is copied below: It is for the matter of submitting a request. I respectfully belong to the association

The entire industry in the city is under the shadow of the current economic downturn. Businesses that cannot maintain operations due to unbearable losses are closing down one after another. The reason for the losses is due to the sluggish business and the sharp reduction in income. However, the selling price of full goods is only 60% of the pawned capital, which is the biggest fatal injury. For example, the average value of full goods pawned each year is 10,000 yuan. The selling price is only 12,000 yuan, which means a loss of 8,000 yuan. In addition, the expenses are insufficient, and the annual consumption exceeds 10,000 yuan. Relying entirely on the meager interest income, how can we make up for the loss and maintain the business? If this continues, if we do not

seek to save it urgently, the whole body will collapse and all businesses will close down in less than a year. The pawn industry, which is the lifeblood of the economic turnover of ordinary people, has this hidden anxiety in its future, and its impact on social people's livelihood is enormous. The association has realized this and submitted a request to your bureau on July 14 last year, requesting approval to shorten the maturity period of pawned goods to 12 months. Later, it was approved that the case was forwarded to the municipal government for review, which led to its indefinite shelving. Now, the bleak situation of the industry is becoming more and more dangerous. It is even more urgent to find ways to remedy it. Therefore, we dare to reiterate the previous request, hoping to benefit the late years. According to the maturity period of half a year in those years, the market was stable,

The secret of balanced prices has no relation. Today, financial resources are exhausted and prices are soaring. The pawned goods are still stored for a long time according to the rules. One day, the pawners abandon them and do not buy them. The clothes, which account for the majority of full goods, have become outdated due to changes in styles and are no longer considered. In addition, the price of raw materials is lower than the pawned capital. How can we seek not to suffer losses and sell them? Moreover, according to the statistics of the industry's redemption volume, less than one in ten people redeem after more than ten months. This proves that the preservation after ten months is a burden for pawn shops.

Capital is stuck in turnover and interest is charged. When selling, it suffers even greater losses. For the pawners, it is of no benefit. Not only is it not practical for both parties, but it is also a waste of resources. Therefore, shortening the maturity period is the key to the current relief of the pawn industry, and it cannot be delayed. Therefore, we dare to not be afraid of the cost of words, and express the situation in detail. We humbly request the hook bureau to forward it to the municipal government and quickly approve the previous case in order to relieve the difficulties of the merchants and benefit the people's livelihood. We are sincerely waiting for orders. We respectfully present to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau.

is concubinage, why do you say that you and Ruan are officially married? What evidence can you provide to prove it? The original letter is recorded below. "To Whom It May Concern, according to a presentation from the Second District Branch of this Association: 'Recently, we received a letter from the Customs Broker Association stating that members like Zhengda, Taikoo Chang, Xingtai Chang, Litai Chang, and Tongju Jiang, and other customs brokers claimed that the French Municipal Council mistakenly thought that we were running apartments. After ordering us to pay this donation in November of last year, the matter was resolved after repeated negotiations. However, the Municipal Council brought up the old matter again after half a year, cutting off the electricity lines of Customs Brokers such as Litai Chang, Zhengda, and Taikoo Chang in May. At a time when the market is so depressed, our colleagues are struggling to make a living. The Municipal Council has made unexpected demands, causing trouble and harming the citizens' peace and order. We are also citizens and ask your association to transfer a letter to the Citizen's Association, seeking their assistance in upholding justice and striving for the Municipal Council on reasonable grounds to stabilize the business.' Accordingly, after investigating that the customs brokers sublet the remaining houses and goods to out-of-town offices in Shanghai, their nature is no different from that of second or third-level tenants, and they are absolutely different from public houses, so there is no reason to pay donations. Moreover, business is so sluggish that it is difficult to solve life's problems, so how can such an unexpected burden be added? As for water and electricity, which are related to the lives of the people, the Municipal Council suddenly cut them off, which is tantamount to putting our citizens to death. Your association is the leader of the citizens and has always been committed to protecting legal rights. It is appropriate to send a letter according to the circumstances, and humbly ask you to uphold justice, help as much as possible, strive for reason, maintain the market and protect public security. In light of this, we have prepared a letter for your perusal, and hope that you will investigate." Therefore, after investigating that the customs brokers sublet the remaining houses and goods to out-of-town offices in Shanghai, completely for business convenience, their nature is indeed different from that of apartments. Now, your bureau wants to collect donations based on apartments, and suddenly cut off water and electricity. This kind of action is excessively oppressive. According to the previous letter, it is appropriate to send a letter to you, hoping that you will consider the difficulties of business, stop the donation, and immediately restore electricity to maintain business and friendship. To the Municipal Council."

It is reported that the company has appointed Wang Dehuai and Sun Guangyu to Nanjing to prepare for the establishment of a branch company in order to expand its business, which will soon begin operations. According to Mr. Shen Zonglian, the Chinese manager of the company, the company has always invested the premiums it collects in domestic businesses, because the interest rate in our country is higher than overseas, and it avoids exchange losses and has never remitted funds abroad. In fact, the Canadian head office still remits funds to China for investment every year.
