The New Medicine Industry Association invited leaders from all walks of life in this city to visit the health exhibition at the New World on the 23rd of this month. They also hired a performance troupe to perform, and many people attended. The China-France Pharmacy distributed Longhu Pi Rendan to everyone on the spot, and those who received it said that the efficacy of this dan was comparable to that of foreign loans, and the value was much cheaper. They all advocated purchasing and using it to save profits.

Era Cartoon Issue 18 Published 168

The Era Cartoon, published by the Era Bookstore Company at No. 300, Simalu, Shanghai, has been around for a year and a half since its first issue was published. The number of copies sold has been increasing with each issue. It is said that the writers of the magazine include excellent writers from all over the country, gathering masterpieces. For example, Lu Zhen's "Adventures in a Silent Country," Liu Shuofu's "Saying Phlegm," Lao Ji's "Silver Jubilee in Hong Kong," etc. Ye Qianyu, who has returned from his northern travels, has quick sketches of the characters in the ancient city in this issue, with clear lines, which are very rare. Each copy is priced at two cents, and all bookstores and newsstands sell them.

Su Farmers Bank Sets Up an Office in Beiqiao; Since Last Month, it has Handled the Shanghai County Treasury 169

Since Shanghai County moved to Beiqiao, Xinhua Savings Bank has set up an office in Beiqiao. In addition to operating business locally, it also acted as an agent for the county treasury. Now, the Shanghai County Treasury has been changed to the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank. Therefore, the bank has set up a Beiqiao office in the same building as the Xinhua office. It will start handling treasury matters on the first of next month. The transfer has been carried out on the 30th of this month. The original business of the Xinhua office will continue as usual, and the time will be extended to provide thorough service.

Songfeng Ancient and Modern Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition 170

The Songfeng Calligraphy and Painting Society of Songjiang is now exhibiting an exhibition of ancient and modern calligraphy and paintings on the second floor of the New World on Nanjing Road. Yesterday was the first day, and the number of visitors was quite crowded. There are hundreds of ancient paintings such as Dong Qichang's landscapes, Sun Kehong's flowers, and Zhang Hong's figures. Modern paintings include Wang Zhilin's and Yu Xiaolian's landscapes, Tang Yangfang's ladies, Zhang Xiaoshi's animals and Buddhas, Zhang Zhuocheng, Li Zhongjie, Huang Shixiang, Sang Boyin, Lou Yuqing, Xue Shifang's flowers, and other works, including vertical scrolls and fan surfaces, hundreds of pieces, which are dazzling and beautiful, making people reluctant to leave. It is said that the exhibition will last for many days, and it will be changed every day. Dozens of pieces were ordered yesterday. All those who share the same interests should go and appreciate them.

Wuxing Fellow Countrymen Initiate Theatrical Performances to Raise Funds for Wupu Vocational Training Center 172

Wuxing County Wupu Migrant Vocational Training Center has been established for many years, providing relief to homeless migrants and teaching them vocational skills. At a time when unemployment is increasing, the establishment of the center is beneficial to society. However, there is a lack of funds, and the whole depends on the proceeds of handicraft products. Recently, due to the commercial decline, the sales of products have been greatly affected, the income and expenditure are disparate, and it is difficult to support. Fellow countrymen in Shanghai initiated theatrical performances to raise funds. On June 17th, a gathering of famous Peking opera artists in Shanghai was invited to perform Peking opera for one day at the Grand Theatre. The stage was generously provided by Lu Liankui and Shen Changgeng. It is said that all sectors have expressed sympathy, and the sale of tickets will definitely be enthusiastic.

The Xujiahui Astronomical Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday said that the sky was clear around Shandong, and a strong breeze was coming from the southwest to the west. Endangering Public Morality and Abandonment and Injury: Both Charges Withdrawn; Both Cases Dismissed Due to Non-Appearance 177

Fei Xinfu, a Ningbo native and owner of the Cheng Yu Cotton Fabric Store at No. 10, Lane 179, Tianjin Road, was recently sued in the First Special District Court by Zhou Li, a Ningbo woman residing at No. 4, Fengrui Lane, Beihai Road, Baker Road, along with her daughter Zhou Suzhen, on charges of endangering public morality. The facts alleged that Yu Meitian, a friend of Zhou Li's husband, was acquainted with Fei. Because of this, Fei became acquainted with Zhou Suzhen and, through Fei's enticement, sexually assaulted her at the New East Hotel in early February of this year. Subsequently, he took her as a concubine, renting a room above the Xiechang New Tobacco Company on Wuzhen Road where they cohabited for two months, after which he disappeared without a trace. Zhou Li sued Fei for rape under Article 140 of the Criminal Code, as her daughter had not reached the legal age. Fei also filed a countersuit, claiming that Zhou Li was a well-known prostitute from Ningbo named Zhilan Abao, and that her two younger sisters, Wenying and Wenlan, were also involved in the sex trade, as was her daughter Zhou Suzhen. Initially, she resided in Room 6 of the Qunyi Hotel. In March, it was rumored that she had moved to Room 225 of the Yingbao Hotel to solicit clients. Fei, through Yu Meitian's introduction, had visited her there. The house on Wuzhen Road was also rented by Zhou Li under the name of Li Wenkui, inviting Fei to come. Fei, due to a lack of funds, refused to go, angering Zhou Li, who demanded 300 yuan from Fei, and upon failing to obtain it, filed a lawsuit, requesting that he be prosecuted for fraud. This case was heard yesterday at 3:00 PM by Judge Wu Zehan of the First Special District Court in the Second Criminal Court. By 3:30 PM, Zhou Li and Zhou Suzhen had not yet reported. Judge Wu ruled that since the plaintiff had been lawfully summoned and had failed to appear without reason, the case should be considered withdrawn. He also advised the defendant's side to withdraw the countersuit as well. Yuan Zhi, the defendant's lawyer, agreed, and Judge Wu ruled that the case was not accepted.

In another case, a woman named Wang Xiuying recently filed a complaint with the First Special District Court, through lawyer Wen Chao, against Xu Hanchen, a senior staff member in the Western Medicine Department of the Jardine Matheson & Co. at No. 110, Sichuan Road, on charges of abandonment and injury. Judge Zhan Liangce accepted the case and scheduled a hearing for 2:30 PM yesterday in the Fifth Criminal Court. Both parties' summonses had been lawfully served, but as of 3:05 PM yesterday, neither party had appeared. Judge Zhan, in accordance with the provisions of the Criminal Procedure Law, declared that the case was not accepted, and the plaintiff's attached civil suit was dismissed.

Education News

Ministry of Education Announces Revision of Secondary School Regulations 178

The Ministry of Education has announced the revision of 121 articles of the secondary school regulations. The original text is as follows:

Chapter 1: General Principles

Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of the Secondary School Law.

Article 2: Secondary schools are places for rigorously training the minds and bodies of young people and cultivating sound citizens. In accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Secondary School Law, they shall implement the following training: (1) Forging strong physiques; (2) Nurturing civic morality; (3) Cultivating national culture; (4) Enhancing life skills; (5) Building a foundation in science; (6) Developing work habits; (7) Inspiring artistic interests.

Article 3: Secondary schools are divided into junior secondary schools and senior secondary schools. The duration of study for each is two years. A school that combines junior and senior secondary education is called a "secondary school." Schools that only offer one level are called "junior secondary schools" or "senior secondary schools."

Article 4: The standard age for students in junior secondary schools is ten to fifteen years old. The standard age for students in senior secondary schools is fifteen to eighteen years old.

Article 5: Public junior and senior secondary schools may separately establish simplified normal courses and special normal courses.

Chapter 2: Establishment and Management

Article 6: The establishment, alteration, and closure of secondary schools established by provinces and cities (referring to municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan) shall first be proposed by the provincial or municipal education administrative organs, with plans or reasons submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval before implementation. The establishment, alteration, and closure of secondary schools established by counties and joint counties shall first be proposed by the responsible education administrative organs, with plans or reasons submitted to the provincial education department for approval before implementation, and then reported to the Ministry for record. The establishment, alteration, and closure of private secondary schools shall be handled in accordance with the procedures stipulated in the private school regulations, with approval from the provincial or municipal education administrative organs, and then reported to the Ministry for record. If the establishment, alteration, and closure of public or private secondary schools do not follow the procedures stipulated in the preceding paragraph, the higher-level education administrative organ may revoke them. The establishment and management of secondary schools affiliated with public or private colleges or universities are the same as those for public or private secondary schools.

Article 7: Provincial secondary schools shall be named after the location where they are situated. County or city secondary schools shall be directly referred to as "the county or city secondary school of X." When there are two or more public secondary schools with the same name in one place, they may be distinguished by numerical order or by using the name of a smaller area as the school name. Jointly established secondary schools shall be called "the joint secondary school of X counties." Private secondary schools shall use a specific name and shall not directly use the name of a location as the school name.

Article 8: Public junior and senior secondary schools may separately establish simplified normal courses and special normal courses only if they meet the following conditions: (1) The original secondary school facilities are complete and teaching equipment is fully equipped. (2) There is a genuine need. (3) The funds are raised separately and are sufficient for operation. (4) Prior approval has been obtained from the competent education administrative organ.

Article 9: Public and private secondary schools shall, within one month after the start of the first semester of each academic year, directly submit or forward the following items to the relevant provincial or municipal education administrative organs for record: (1) Registers of new students, transfer students, returning students, suspended students, dropouts, and students at each level for the current academic year. (2) The academic qualifications, experiences, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time status of the school principal and faculty for the current academic year. (3) The annual budget. (4) Changes to the school rules, school buildings, and equipment for the current academic year. (5) Grade reports of students at each level from the previous academic year. (6) The final accounts or revenue and expenditure items for the previous year. The items in paragraph 2 above shall be reported by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs to the Ministry of Education. A summary table of items 1, 3, 4, 5, and 6 shall also be sent to the Ministry.

Article 10: Public and private secondary schools shall, within one month after the start of the second semester, directly submit or forward the following items to the relevant provincial or municipal education administrative organs for record: (1) Registers of new students, transfer students, returning students, suspended students, and dropouts for the current semester. (2) The academic qualifications, experiences, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time status of newly appointed faculty for the current semester, and the names and reasons for departure of departing faculty. (3) Grade reports of students at each level for the previous semester. The items in paragraph 1 above shall be reported by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs to the Ministry of Education. A summary table of items 2 and 3 shall also be sent to the Ministry.

Article 11: Public and private secondary schools shall, two months before each graduation, prepare the resumes and academic records of graduating students and directly submit or forward them to the provincial or municipal education administrative organs for approval before holding graduation examinations or participating in joint graduation examinations.

Article 12: Public and private secondary schools shall, within one month after each graduation, prepare a graduation grade report of the graduates and directly submit or forward it to the provincial or municipal education administrative organs for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 13: Provincial and municipal education administrative organs shall dispatch inspectors to supervise and guide public and private secondary schools at least once each semester, and submit the inspection and recommendation items to the Ministry of Education for record within one month after the completion of the inspection.

Chapter 3: Funding

Article 14: The start-up, regular, and temporary expenses of provincial and municipal secondary schools shall be provided by provincial and municipal funds. The expenses of county and jointly established secondary schools shall be provided by county funds or the funds of the jointly established counties. The expenses of private secondary schools shall be provided by their school boards.

Article 15: County secondary schools may receive provincial subsidies if the local area is genuinely poor and the school has excellent academic performance. Private secondary schools may not receive public subsidies unless they have genuinely excellent academic performance.

Article 16: The standards for public subsidies to county and private secondary schools shall be determined by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 17: In the distribution of regular expenses for secondary schools, salaries shall not exceed 70%, equipment expenses shall account for at least 20%, and administrative expenses shall not exceed 10%. The budget form will be determined separately.

Article 18: The expenditure of secondary school funds shall strive for thrift and accuracy, and the entire revenue and expenditure situation must be publicly and thoroughly reviewed by the financial audit committee. The audit measures shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and reported to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Chapter 4: Organization

Article 19: Junior and senior secondary school students are divided into first, second, and third grades according to the curriculum progress.

Article 20: The number of students in each grade shall be 50, but there must be at least 25 students.

Article 21: Except for physical education and military training, which may use other grouping methods for teaching, secondary school students shall not be taught in combined classes for any subject.

Article 22: Secondary school students shall be separated by gender in different schools or different classes as a principle.

Article 23: Newly established secondary schools shall not recruit students above the first grade in the first year and shall not recruit third-grade students in the second year.

Chapter 5: Curriculum

Article 24: The teaching subjects for junior secondary schools are civics, physical education, boy scouts, hygiene, Chinese language, English language, mathematics, botany, zoology, chemistry, physics, history, geography, labor, drawing, and music.

Article 25: The teaching subjects for senior secondary schools are civics, physical education, hygiene, military training (military nursing for girls), Chinese language, English language, mathematics, biology, chemistry, physics, Chinese and foreign history, Chinese and foreign geography, ethics, drawing, and music.

Article 26: In secondary schools established in special areas that require Mongolian, Tibetan, or a first foreign language, the teaching subjects in the senior section may be reduced by hygiene, ethics, drawing, and music.

Article 27: To meet local needs and for experimental education, secondary schools may establish vocational subjects, but the establishment of subjects and equipment conditions must first be reported to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Article 28: Secondary school curriculum standards will be determined separately.

Article 29: Secondary school textbooks must use those edited or approved by the Ministry of Education. Teachers' self-compiled materials must conform to the curriculum standards set by the Ministry and must be submitted to the competent education administrative organs for review and reported to the Ministry of Education for record at the end of each semester.

Article 30: Teaching in each subject should make active use of textbooks, adopt local and temporary supplementary teaching materials, and pay attention to experiments and practice. Secondary schools, except for foreign language textbooks, shall use Chinese textbooks and shall not use foreign books. Secondary school teachers shall use Mandarin Chinese as the language of instruction.

Article 31: Teachers should pay attention to the character of students and should inspire their ability to observe and think, as well as the spirit of automatic research.

Article 32: Students in the final year of secondary school may use their holidays for sightseeing trips, but they must not interfere with class time, and the expenses shall be borne by the students themselves. (To be continued)

Ministry of Education Announces Revision of Normal School Regulations 179

The Ministry of Education announced the revision of 143 articles of the Normal School Regulations on the 24th. The original text is as follows:

Chapter 1: General Principles

Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Normal School Law.

Article 2: Normal schools are places for rigorously training the minds and bodies of young people and cultivating sound elementary school teachers. In accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Normal School Law, they shall implement the following training: (1) Forging strong physiques; (2) Nurturing moral character; (3) Cultivating national culture; (4) Enhancing scientific knowledge and skills; (5) Developing work habits; (6) Inspiring interest in research on children's education; (7) Cultivating the spirit of lifelong service to education.

Article 3: Normal schools may establish special normal courses and kindergarten normal courses. Public middle schools and high schools may also establish special normal courses.

Article 4: A normal school that only accepts female students is called a women's normal school. A normal school whose main purpose is to cultivate teachers for rural elementary schools may be called a rural normal school.

Article 5: The duration of study in a normal school is three years. The duration of study in a kindergarten normal course is one or two years. The duration of study in a special normal course is one year.

Article 6: In order to urgently cultivate teachers for vocational education, various localities may establish simplified normal schools or attach simplified normal courses to normal schools and public junior secondary schools. The specific measures will be stipulated in a separate chapter.

Article 7: The age of admission to a normal school shall be fifteen to twenty years old.

Chapter 2: Establishment and Management

Article 8: The establishment, alteration, and closure of normal schools established by provinces and cities (referring to municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan) shall first be proposed by the provincial or municipal education administrative organs, with plans or reasons submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval before implementation. The establishment, alteration, and closure of normal schools established by counties and jointly established counties shall first be proposed by the responsible education administrative organs, with plans or reasons submitted to the provincial education department for approval before implementation, and then reported to the Ministry for record. If the normal schools do not follow the procedures stipulated in the preceding paragraph, the higher-level education administrative organ may revoke them.

Article 9: Normal schools should be located in cities or villages depending on local conditions, and should be located in rural areas as much as possible.

Article 10: The provincial education departments may, according to the situation in each province, divide the entire province into several normal school districts. One normal school and one women's normal school may be established in each normal school district. The normal schools mentioned in the preceding paragraph should first recruit students from the counties within the district.

Article 11: Provincial normal schools shall be named after the location where they are situated. County or city normal schools shall be directly referred to as "the county or city normal school of X." When there are two or more normal schools with the same name in one place, they may be distinguished by numerical order or by using the name of a smaller area as the school name. Jointly established normal schools shall be called "the joint normal school of X counties."

Article 12: Normal schools shall, within one month after the start of the first semester of each academic year, directly submit or forward the following items to the relevant provincial or municipal education administrative organs for record: (1) Registers of new students, transfer students, returning students, suspended students, dropouts, and students at each level for the current academic year. (2) The academic qualifications, experiences, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time status of the school principal and faculty for the current academic year. (3) The annual budget. (4) Changes to the school rules, school buildings, and equipment for the current academic year. (5) Grade reports of students at each level from the previous academic year. (6) The final accounts or revenue and expenditure items for the previous year. (7) The service and school guidance situation of graduates from the previous academic year. The items in paragraph 2 above shall be reported by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs to the Ministry of Education. A summary table of items 1, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 shall also be sent to the Ministry.

Article 13: Normal schools shall, within one month after the start of the second semester, directly submit or forward the following items to the relevant provincial or municipal education administrative organs for record: (1) Registers of new students, transfer students, returning students, suspended students, and dropouts for the current semester. (2) The academic qualifications, experiences, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time status of newly appointed faculty for the current semester, and the names and reasons for departure of departing faculty. (3) Grade reports of students at each level for the previous semester. The items in paragraph 1 above shall be reported by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs to the Ministry of Education. A summary table of items 2 and 3 shall also be sent to the Ministry.

Article 14: Normal schools shall, two months before each graduation, prepare the resumes and academic records of graduating students and directly submit or forward them to the provincial or municipal education administrative organs for approval before holding graduation examinations or participating in joint graduation examinations.

Article 15: Normal schools shall, within one month after each graduation, prepare a graduation grade report of the graduates and measures for distribution of service and directly submit or forward them to the provincial or municipal education administrative organs for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 16: Provincial and municipal education administrative organs shall dispatch inspectors to supervise and guide normal schools at least once each semester, and submit the inspection and recommendation items to the Ministry of Education for record within one month after the completion of the inspection.

Chapter 3: Funding

Article 17: The start-up, regular, and temporary expenses of provincial and municipal normal schools shall be provided by provincial and municipal funds. The expenses of county and jointly established normal schools shall be provided by county funds or the funds of the jointly established counties.

Article 18: County normal schools may receive provincial subsidies if the local area is genuinely poor and the school has excellent academic performance.

Article 19: The standards for provincial subsidies to county normal schools shall be determined by the provincial education department and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 20: In the distribution of regular expenses for normal schools, except for student meals, salaries shall not exceed 70%, equipment expenses shall account for at least 20%, and administrative expenses shall not exceed 10%. The budget form will be determined separately.

Article 21: The expenditure of normal school funds shall strive for thrift and accuracy, and the entire revenue and expenditure situation must be publicly and thoroughly reviewed by the financial audit committee. The audit measures shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and reported to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Chapter 4: Organization

Article 22: Normal school students, except for special normal course students, are divided into first, second, and third grades according to the curriculum progress and the duration of each course.

Article 23: The number of students in each grade shall be 50, but there must be at least 25 students.

Article 24: Except for physical education and military training, which may use other grouping methods for teaching, normal school students shall not be taught in combined classes for any subject.

Article 25: Normal school students shall be separated by gender in different schools or different classes as a principle.

Article 26: Newly established normal schools shall not recruit students above the first grade in the first year and shall not recruit third-grade students in the second year.

Suzhou Women's Normal School Dismisses Principal Due to Exam Boycott; Education Department Orders Early Holiday Immediately 180

The entire student body of the Provincial Suzhou Women's Normal School, in opposition to Principal Chen Shu, launched a wave of dismissal agitation. The details of the incident have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The Education Department sent Secretary Huang, Section Chief Xiang, and Section Member Xue to Suzhou to investigate. The investigation results were reported to the Education Department and filed on record. On the 24th, Secretary Huang went to the school to supervise the examination, but the entire student body boycotted the examination because the goal of dismissing the principal had not been achieved. Secretary Huang immediately telegraphed the province for instructions. That afternoon, a reply from Director Zhou was received, instructing five urgent handling measures: (1) Expel ten students who were found to be ringleaders and coerced their classmates; (2) Start the holiday early from today, and carefully inform each parent to take their students home. No food or accommodation will be provided from the 26th onward; (3) Students who were coerced and blindly followed will be allowed to reform themselves; (4) Those who incited the disturbance will be specifically reported for investigation; (5) Principal Chen Shu is known to be strict with discipline and has excellent performance, so she should diligently manage affairs and not be discouraged. After receiving the telegram, Secretary Huang, accompanied by the Wu County Magistrate, led police to the school and ordered the students to take the examination according to the law. However, no one took the examination. Therefore, students Wu Wenzao (president of the student government), Jian Xiuying, Qian Xiufang (vice president), Sun De, Zhu Guangxi, Ding Ruifen, Zhu Yueying, Xu Wanling, Yao Tongzhu, Chu Jiayuan, and Zhang Lǜxi were expelled. On the morning of yesterday (the 25th), Secretary Huang, in accordance with the instructions of the Education Department, announced the early holiday. Therefore, local students returned home separately that day, and other out-of-town students are also preparing to return home. Secretary Huang, together with Principal Chen, are carefully identifying the coerced students in order to report to the Education Department and request instructions for rectification.

Ministry of Education Instruction: Improve Lingnan University (Private) 183

On the 25th, the Ministry of Education issued an instruction to Lingnan University (Private), stating in brief, "The school has been inspected by personnel and reports have been submitted. After review, the school's allocation of funds is able to focus on equipment, and most teachers are full-time and diligent in their duties. Teaching practice is also considered genuine, and research work is able to focus on practical issues. The achievements of the sericulture department in the study of sericulture and the biology department in the collection of plant and insect specimens are particularly commendable. However, the following points still need to be improved: 1. The school's funding is already difficult, and it is insufficient to manage the current scale. The number of students in each department is also not large. The school should reduce its scope, enrich its content, and if there is a need to establish a home economics or fine arts department, change it to a specialized course. The names of the social science departments are too broad and should be corrected according to their actual scope. The pre-medical department has already been ordered to be abolished by the Ministry and should be closed immediately. The school should submit a plan to reduce each department within June for approval. 2. The various regulations established by the school, such as the organizational outline and school rules, are not in line with the University Organization Law, the University Regulations, and various educational laws. They should be revised and submitted to the Ministry for approval and implementation. The position of consultant is not based on the University Organization Law and should be abolished immediately. Important officials within the school should be appointed with Chinese scholars. The classification and naming of faculty should also be revised. 3. The name and methods of the graduate research institute established by the school are not fully in line with the Provisional Organizational Regulations for University Graduate Institutes promulgated by the Ministry last year. If the school needs to establish research institutes, it should follow the above-mentioned regulations and formulate a plan based on the school's faculty, equipment, and funding situation and submit it to the Ministry for approval. Before being approved, the school may not recruit graduate students or award advanced degrees. 4. The school lacks a foundation and relies heavily on tuition fees for its recurring expenses, which is not a sustainable plan. The school board should raise funds to increase revenue. The student fees are too numerous and the amounts are too high, and they should be reduced. The school's established joint school system, which provides exemptions from entrance examinations for graduates of joint schools, is inappropriate and should be abolished immediately to prevent abuse. 5. The school lacks active measures for moral education, and student attire is particularly extravagant. The moral education committee should be responsible for strictly formulating methods to correct this. It is hereby ordered that you strictly follow these instructions and report the results accordingly."

The Public Works Department's Financial Difficulties Affect Education and Construction in the Concession 185

The Public Works Department has recently felt financially constrained, making it difficult to proceed with educational facilities within the concession. For example, the Western Girls' Public School on Yuyuan Road urgently needs a home science building, and the Western Primary School in the neighborhood also requires an assembly hall. However, due to lack of funds, both projects have had to be temporarily shelved. The construction costs for these two projects are estimated at 35,000 yuan for the former and 25,000 yuan for the latter, both of which have been included in this year's budget. However, due to financial constraints, they have had to be postponed along with other new constructions already included in the budget. However, during a previous Public Works Department board meeting, the Director-General stated that the construction of the Western Primary School assembly hall was originally planned as part of the existing building, but has been delayed until now due to economic reasons. He also noted that the construction of the Girls' Public School's home science building is particularly necessary, as the school originally had a building with home economics and cooking classes. However, the building was demolished as it obstructed the construction of the neighboring Western Primary School. Therefore, it is now urgent to rebuild it to meet immediate needs. This is an important part of restoring the school's original building, and should not be compared to newly added constructions like the Western Primary School's assembly hall. The Education Department is also willing to continue its efforts to promote the matter, so that construction can begin as soon as funds become available. However, given the current situation, it is feared that this will be difficult to achieve in the short term.

Public Works Department Stipulates Use of Subsidies for Chinese Schools in the Concession 186

The Public Works Department's Education Department recently raised the issue of how subsidies for various private Chinese schools are used for discussion at the board meeting. According to the Education Department, some schools have used the subsidies to reduce or waive tuition fees for students with excellent academic performance and conduct who come from poor families. While this use cannot be considered inappropriate, it is questionable whether it aligns with the original purpose of the subsidy. According to the Education Department, the use of the subsidy should be limited to the following three categories: (1) rent and property taxes; (2) maintenance and upkeep of buildings and equipment; and (3) staff salaries. Although it may be difficult to rectify the past practices of the schools concerned, from now on, after receiving the subsidy, each school should handle it in accordance with the above three uses and should not divert it to other uses, which would cause inconvenience. The matter was discussed and approved for implementation at the board meeting on the 24th of this month. Furthermore, according to a report by the Director of Education and the Director of Health, a total of 176 private Chinese schools were found to be qualified and should be granted subsidies this spring. Twelve schools were cancelled or not granted subsidies. The reasons for not granting subsidies to the latter twelve schools were that seven schools failed to provide sufficient evidence of expenditure in the previous year, three schools were making insufficient progress, one school was unqualified, and the remaining school had promised to rebuild the school building last year but has not yet done so. The above schools have been listed by the Public Works Department's Education Department and submitted to the board for approval.

New Life Movement Promotion Association Promotes New Student Life Fans and Asks Education Bureau to Order Schools to Purchase 187

Chun Qiu (Spring and Autumn)

Tidbits 196

— （倪尙龍）(Ni Shanglong)

Whenever I hear, write, or see "Spring and Autumn," I always feel endless sadness in my heart. Because when the swallows leave, there is a time for them to return; when the flowers wither, there is a time for them to bloom again; when the grass and trees wither, there is a time for them to flourish again. But the Spring and Autumn seasons that we waste will never return!

In winter, hands are most afraid of being cold. If you put your hands in cold water again, you will feel particularly cold and painful, but as soon as you take them out of the cold water, you will soon feel warm. This is a wonderful lesson of "Only by enduring the greatest hardships can you become a great person."

A young man who grows up in luxury, or a young man who grows up relying on others and does not need to work for food, or a young man who is spoiled from childhood, rarely has great abilities. Compared to poor children, he is like a flower cultivated in a greenhouse, compared to a palm tree whose every branch must endure the beatings of storms.

Gardener 197

— 耘 殮 (Yun Lian)

Flowers are loved by everyone, and everyone is willing to appreciate them, cultivate their mind, and temper their temperament. Even scenic areas with clear mountains and waters ultimately need them to embellish them. Elegant ladies regard flowers as life, and even simple village girls like to pick a wild flower and insert it in their messy temples. Peng Zeling's appreciation of chrysanthemums in Dongli became a timeless story. An ancient person wrote about the scenery of West Lake in March, with the line "The light of the flowers is like cheeks, the ripples of the waves are like mirrors." Is it not that in Hangzhou, where the mountains and rivers are the best in the world, flowers also occupy an important part? Nowadays, social customs dictate that flower wreaths be offered at funerals, and flower baskets be given to celebrate birthdays. In fact, these techniques are purely artificial embellishments, exquisite operations, not from the hands of artists, but from the ingenuity of clumsy floral clerks. City parks, private villas, and educational institutions with the advantage of gardens all bear the footprints of gardeners: they are dressed plainly, have a peaceful mind, and are not at all impatient, as quiet as a virgin, as careful as a hair, unlike ordinary laborers. Therefore, from morning to night, from spring to winter, they spend their lives moving flowers and grafting trees in a peaceful atmosphere. Eight or nine out of ten of them are from the counties of Hangzhou and Jinhua, as if they have a gang, which can echo the Yangzhou barbers and the Chongming charter drivers. The higher wages are 30 or 40 yuan per month, and the average is about 10 yuan. If A finds a client with a higher salary, this old rice bowl will be transferred to another peer. To put it nicely, it is to promote the younger generation and promote friendship between fellow villagers, but in fact it is a "Monroe Doctrine practitioner." They do not envy prosperity, but live in wealthy families. No matter how much the social economy collapses, these masters of the gardens will never discount their wages, affecting the price of their labor. On good days in spring and autumn, the red flowers are brightly colored, the green leaves are fresh and dripping, and the yellow stamens are clearly painted. The shallow grasses are green as a lawn. These scenes, which receive the praise of everyone, are their comfort. Gardener, gardener, you truly deserve to be called "flower protector."

Old Gun 198

— 寒玉 (Han Yu)

The corner of Xizang Road and Baker Road is the station for several university buses, and many university students stay there. Therefore, many newspaper vendors do business there. The most eye-catching is "Old Gun."

His face is terribly thin, which is obviously a characteristic of special hobbies, so everyone calls him "Old Gun." After a long time, he also named himself "Old Gun."

"Old Gun" has special skills in selling newspapers. When people just arrive to wait for the bus, he approaches them and says, "Sir! The ×× bus will arrive in just a few minutes. Since you have nothing to do standing here, buy an evening paper to read!" People accept his suggestion and buy one. His price is one copper coin more expensive than usual. He knows that university students will not care about these.

"Old Gun" can not only contact students, but also contact the personnel on the school buses. When they are backing up, he pays attention for them; he also tells them the time. Therefore, he can go to the bus to sell newspapers. People sitting on the bus can always hear these words every day: "Sir, when you go, don't forget to buy ×× evening paper!"

After a business is successful, someone will come to compete. "Old Gun"'s newspaper sales are no exception. The number of newspaper vendors suddenly increased, and their prices were cheaper, which was indeed a great blow to him. His method of resistance was to abandon shouting "Da Wan Evening News, New Evening News," and use special eloquence to deal with the students. In this way, he defeated all these competitors.

But there are times when "Old Gun"'s business is not good. During summer and winter vacations, many students leave school, and the school bus business is particularly quiet, and his business is the same. Therefore, he always says when the holidays are coming: "When school is on vacation, the gentlemen can go back, but Old Gun is unlucky." Now that the summer vacation is coming again, "Old Gun"'s unlucky days are approaching.

Free Teahouse 199

— 方正 (Fang Zheng)

You won't find fashionable people here. There are only simple farmers and loyal farmers. Strong physiques and rough hands and feet are their only means of production. What is modern? What is patriotism? They never understand. But they are very devoted to mud and wood carvings of gods, so the entire rural area is caught in a vortex of superstition.

Their daily recreational venue after work is a small free teahouse. The so-called free teahouse is not a real teahouse, but the entrance of a small butcher shop, where a few stools and two modified broken tables become a free teahouse. Teapots are prepared by each person, so they can start talking. What is the content of the conversation? It is truly unbearable to listen to. It is not the old news of Emperor Guangxu, but stories of gods and monsters and martial heroes.

Occasionally, there are a few people who return to the countryside from the city, and they always enthusiastically advise them not to talk about those old and corrupt ghost stories. It is no longer that era. They will curl their lips and answer, "You are strange! Aren't you afraid of ××× on the List of Fengshen?" So new knowledge can never be poured into their brains.

Now Shanghai is promoting a literacy campaign. People who are unable to attend school and are illiterate now have the opportunity to be educated! This is certainly a good thing. But what about those ignorant farmers! I hope the authorities will pay more attention to them! It is best to set up a small public education center in the rural area, so that they can go to the education center to read books during their spare time. They will not only receive unlimited new knowledge, but also get rid of those unnecessary superstitions. Or send investigators to the countryside to conduct a field survey to find out how many illiterate people there are, and then send teachers to guide them. That would be very beneficial!

An Imperial Aroma: Memoirs of the Princess, by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou 200

The heavy rain was lashing madly at the great palaces built along the edge of Longevity Hill, and with the darkness of the sky, the rain was falling in silver-threaded curtains. Under the eaves of several of the palaces, the light was so dim that the eunuchs moving about appeared as nothing but shifting black shadows: almost like the scenes I had witnessed in the ancient palaces in Mukden at night—and like the others in the palace I was panic-stricken and trembling.

The Empress Dowager had been too much fatigued from her excursion on the lake yesterday evening, and, having taken a bit of cold, was feeling poorly with a cough; and when Her Old Majesty was uncomfortable, her temper was always very terrible:—so when the Empress Dowager was ill we were always very much worried and dared not forget for a moment that we existed and breathed only at her pleasure; a mere whim could stop us from existing and prevent us from breathing. As a matter of fact, I think all of us, men and women, at these times could not help considering Her Old Majesty as a kind of terrible old ogre who could injure our lives with ease: at least myself and the other ladies-in-waiting, and the eunuchs who were constantly in attendance, and Kuang Hsü and Lung Yu and several others who were more closely associated with her Old Majesty were of this way of thinking! However, at all events, I could flatter myself that I knew best how to handle her, for, at heart, she had been very kind to me, perhaps on account of my more liberal education, and for this reason she took me into her special favor, and often granted me special privileges absolutely unattainable by others; and besides she was very fond of listening to me talk. (349)

Little Western Paradise 201

— By Zhang Henshui

Fifteenth Chapter: Bitterly Persuading with Earnestness, Not Just Arbitrary Decisions; The Sound of Money and Shadows of Lanterns, Pitifully Selling People

Zhiqian laughed: Paying attention isn't necessarily a bad thing. As the ancients said, "The object of affection lies entirely with us." But times are different now. Everything boils down to economics. Brother, it seems your educational expenses are already quite strained. If you have such a burden on your back, I can't bear to think about what might happen in the future. As he said this, Zhiqian's attitude was very calm. He fixed his eyes on Beihai, who was standing in the middle of the room, unable to utter a word. He looked down at his hands, secretly smoothing his clothes. Zhiqian said: You might have misunderstood, thinking I'm also pursuing this woman. Didn't I just tell you? My relationship with my wife is very good. If I were to take a concubine, wouldn't my wife and I get divorced? That would be a bad deal for me. Beihai, in his haste, couldn't find a suitable word to explain himself, so he raised his neck and replied with the words "a joke." After saying those two words, he continued to stand there. Zhiqian laughed: If that girl Ruochu is bought by someone named Jia, not only would you feel bad, but I would also feel sorry for her. However, eavesdropping outside when they're discussing things is not appropriate. No matter what his attitude towards us is, that man named Jia has been glaring at us. My suggestion is that you sit here with me for a while. Soon, Miss Yang will go to the Hu's house to get a reply. At that time, I'll pull her aside and ask a few questions to get a general idea. Beihai smiled faintly: What will we do if we find out? And what if we don't? Zhiqian laughed: Do you think we have any other options besides this? (249)

Short Story

Cast Iron Woodworm 202

— Juanlong

Manhui was a pockmarked man with lips thicker than most. When he smiled, his triangular eyes narrowed into thin slits. In the village, he was quite a character. He was famous because of his pockmarks, thick lips, and triangular eyes. When trouble arose, he could take down several people single-handedly. He possessed a natural talent for scheming. As soon as his wife told him the rice jar was empty, he'd immediately borrow two dollars from somewhere to buy rice. But the day he would repay the money was very dim. Creditors didn't dare ask him to pay up. Otherwise, he would just puff up his thick lips, pop out his triangular eyes, and launch into a bout of boasting about how great he was, which would suffice to deal with the debt collection for the time being. The money and property he had openly and secretly taken from close relatives and neighbors was too much to calculate. Almost everyone in the village was in debt to him... Therefore, besides calling him "Old Scoundrel Pockface" behind his back, people also gave him a nickname: "Cast Iron Woodworm."

People had to rely on their own hard work to make a living year-round, but he could get by by boring here and there like a cast iron woodworm. He could even find food to eat in cast iron. He wasn't seen barefoot in the fields for more than a few days out of the year, yet he lived a more comfortable life than others. He had fish and meat for every meal and brewed several jars of wine. After each meal, he would take a pot, drink his fill, and then go to the neighborhood to boast. Everyone in the village was afraid of his ferocity, so they had no choice but to treat him like a local god, which made him puff up his thick lips, happily turning his triangular eyes into two thin slits.

The dry goods store in the neighborhood had been owing him a substantial amount of money for a long time. When the end of the year arrived, and people were desperately trying to find a way out, he would put on his pockmarked face, and smile with his triangular eyes narrowed to thin slits, and go to the boss:

"Old Song, you've been too busy these past few days! Let me collect some debts for you!"

"Ah! No, I don't need it! I wouldn't dare! You're busy too!" Old Guan knew that he was up to his old tricks again, and could only secretly lament in his heart: "He wants to buy on credit again!"

The New Year was the period when gambling was at its most intense. Although debt collectors were pressing people for money at home all day long, he still spent his days gambling, half avoiding debt and half gambling. When he lost all his money and returned home, he would vent his anger by scolding and beating his wife or daughter.

Perhaps he had done too much evil in his life. Now that he was over forty years old, he still had no son. No one in the village failed to secretly curse him behind his back: "Heaven has eyes! This kind of person will never have a son, and he'll get what's coming to him!" But the "Cast Iron Woodworm" himself said it was just bad luck, so he desperately ate vegetarian food on the first and fifteenth of each month. On major festivals or the birthdays of Guanyin and Buddha, he and his wife would piously follow the other Buddhist women to temples to burn incense and sit through the night. He would even wear straw sandals and bring some rice to trek fifty or sixty miles to the Great Buddha Temple for the festival... But Guanyin Bodhisattva still refused to give him a son!

He had used his "Cast Iron Woodworm" skills to scheme several times over the inheritance or division of property of close relatives. When his older brother and fourth younger brother died, he swallowed up their two shares of the inheritance. When his second younger brother died, fortunately, he had a son. Although he couldn't seize that share of the property, he still managed to cheat and take a considerable amount. When the sister-in-law of his neighbor A Xiang died (her husband had died early), that property should have been inherited by A Xiang's eldest son. But because she had a scandalous affair with the "Cast Iron Woodworm," the "Cast Iron Woodworm" took the opportunity to make the property fall apart early on. By the time she died and A Xiang's eldest son inherited it, he discovered that only four-tenths of the property remained! Although A Xiang understood perfectly well in his heart, he could only dare to be angry but not speak out!

When the City God Temple was to be renovated, he used his scheming skills to wrangle the position of person in charge, ostensibly to fulfill some obligations for the public, but secretly he was desperately filling his pockets! After the temple was renovated, he triumphantly turned up his thick lips in the neighborhood and said:

"After living a lifetime, I've finally done some filial duty for the City God!"

Grains: Wheat Futures Gradually Improving 211

——Spot Prices High and Stable, Medium Prices Flat——

Yesterday's wheat market saw quiet trading in the morning sessions, with little price fluctuation. Foreign wheat prices were only slightly up by 8 to 12 cents. Buyers and sellers within and outside the industry were watching. As the afternoon session opened, market sentiment gradually improved. The flour market was tight, and there was a continuous intention of rain, so the market sentiment tended to be stable. It is expected that the arrival of rain-affected wheat will be difficult to become a reality in the short term, because this year's output is relatively small, and farmers need to prepare for famine, so the prosperity of previous years still has to be waited for. He Xia Rice Frequently Declines 213

——Foreign Rice Sales Also Weak——

Yesterday, Du rice (South Shanghai) arrived from various sources, a total of 25 numbers, (goods total more than 5,000 stone). Apart from a slight increase in purchases on the market, there were no large buyers. Sales were sluggish, and the market showed a downward trend. The prices of various thick Japonica and late rice varieties continued to fall. High-quality rice fell by a small amount, while medium-quality rice fell by about 20 cents. The prices of Yinbian Yuan and Du Jian also fell by 10 to 20 cents. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, 17 or 18 shipments arrived from He Xia. Sales on the market remained weak. White Japonica rice fell by another 10 cents, thin rice and early Japonica rice fell by 10 to 20 cents, white yuan rice fell by 10 cents, and other varieties also fell by small amounts of several cents to a dime.

Yesterday's foreign rice market saw a decrease in sales. The mainland has been shipping goods for months, and local demand is sufficient. Ports such as Huzhou, Zhaxhi, and other ports along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway are overstocked. After the rain, everyone is busy with farming, and demand is even weaker. Yesterday, shipments to the Yangtze River area and the northern ports were suspended. Only inland areas within the city slightly responded. The entire market only opened less than 5,000 bags. With weak sales, the market immediately cut prices by 3 cents. New orders continue to arrive in Shanghai, and a turnaround is expected only when sales in various areas become active. However, the upstream of the Yangtze River already has too much rain, and the future market cannot yet be grasped.

Yesterday the transaction was not lonely and total sales of cakes even approached 10,000 cakes. Yellow beans once turned up, but was only for a brief time, and there was exhaustion. Transactions were instantly tightened. Factories had already made big volume orders of date-beans, so now beans were not needed. Free Talk

On Wu Jianren's Novels 219

— Han Feng

Wu Jianren, a native of Foshan, like Li Boyuan, the head of Nan Ting, did not publish any systematic theory about novels. What can be found now are only some scattered short articles, scattered in various magazines at that time. To talk about his understanding of novels based on his views on novels, these are the only materials.

The most important one is the "Preface to Monthly Novels," in which he presents his views on novels head-on. In addition to agreeing with Liang Qichao's "The Relationship Between Novels and Governance," recognizing the importance of novels, he added two meanings: one is "sufficient to supplement memory," and the other is "easy to input knowledge." His reason is that "profound and difficult-to-understand articles" are "not as easy for readers as shallow and interesting ones," and using novels to input knowledge will make readers "remember history and reason easily." In summary, novels are the easiest to spread widely and the most capable of moving people. He advocates "borrowing the fun and emotion of novels as an aid to moral education."

This view, as seen today, is really too ordinary, but at the time when we were beginning to understand the importance of novels, when "strange and disjointed" works were constantly produced, this statement was enough to correct many bad tendencies and emphasize readers' understanding of the relationship between novels and governance.

He pays special attention to historical novels. He wrote "Romance of the Two Jins" and "Painful History" (Romance of the Southern Song), but unfortunately neither was completed. According to his opinion, it is said that classics are difficult to attract people's attention because of their complex beginnings and endings, profound texts, and voluminous volumes. To make the content of these high-level classics universally and deeply rooted in the masses, it is only possible to use the style of romance. Only the words of novelists are interesting and can attract people, can supplement the inadequacy of textbooks, and can make "novels accompany official history to gallop, and official history use novels as a guide" (General Preface to Historical Novels.)

He is quite dissatisfied with the old historical novels. He said that many of them are capable of contrivance, but instead make the truth of history hidden and obscure, and there are many absurd things, which makes "the foolish even more foolish." He eloquently discusses this type of novel:

"I have often silently calculated that from the Spring and Autumn Period to the Chronicles of Heroes and the Iron Crown Chart, except for the States, those that are contrived account for 99 percent. Some even borrow the name of an ancient person as the main brain of a book, and everything except the name of this main brain is contrived. For example, the Chronicles of the Eastern Conquest writing about Xue Rengui, and the Wanhualou writing about Di Qing. As for the Investiture of the Gods, which uses mythological tales and borrows history for attachment, it goes without saying. The Eastern and Western Han Dynasties are also too brief and lack interest, and they cannot avoid falling into the talk of falsehoods and contrivances. The Eastern and Western Jin Dynasties are not complete and do not fit the style. Literary scholars see them and say that there is official history, why should I read this; those who know a little see them and say that I don't understand this, so it is like having no novels." (Preface to the Romance of the Two Jins)

He believes that these are not the right track of historical novels and should not avoid historical facts, so he wants to devote his greatest efforts to the creation of works in this area. Starting from this understanding, he also pays attention to drum lyrics and ballad singing. He once re-published Jia Fuxi's drum lyrics and wrote a preface for it. He also formally discussed ballad singing novels in a new novel:

"Ballad singing songbooks are called wooden fish books by the Cantonese. Although these wooden fish books are all contrived and unfounded, their main purpose is to talk about loyalty, filial piety, and righteousness. Even when telling the story of a prostitute, they must say that she died for love. Other things such as righteous servants taking the blame for their masters and filial daughters selling themselves to redeem their fathers are all over the place and cannot be denied, and there must be a very good ending. Women and girls who are accustomed to reading these books are educated, and customs also become better because of this. It is a pity that these wooden fish books are rich in dialects and cannot be spread far."

He even attributes the non-licentiousness of Cantonese customs to ballad singing novels. Wu Jianren was a supporter of old morality, so this method is not surprising, but his ability to value these "lower-class books" that were looked down upon by the general public is unmatched. This kind of understanding is similar to that of Li Boyuan.

Some novel reviews at that time were often not objective. For example, it was said that Water Margin was a socialist book, that Pu Songling was an anti-foreign family, and that he specialized in nationalism, and that the Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio faction all referred to Manchus. Wu Jianren did not think so. He raised objections several times. For example, he commented on Water Margin:

"For example, the Water Margin, records the harm of robbers, but today's people often say that it advocates egalitarianism. I am afraid that Shi Nai'an would never have had this idea at that time. However, he described these 108 people gathering in Liangshanpo, just like a present state of an egalitarian society. I have read it repeatedly, and I think it is a work of anger at the world. Our country has never had the saying of freedom of speech, and writing is always easy to cause trouble. Therefore, the heart of worrying about the times and being angry at the world has to be entrusted to novels, and even when entrusted to novels, one dare not write about it explicitly, but must use euphemisms and metaphors as allegories. This is the plight of the ancients writing books. The Water Margin is a separate cut of a biography of corrupt officials."

This is relatively objective, unlike others who forcibly pull it into the realm of modern thought. Therefore, he has a saying: "Although I do not want to use the ideals of the ancients to break into the ideals of today." He commented on Flowers in the Mirror, believing it to be "adding an annotation to the Classic of Mountains and Seas," calling it an ideal novel and a science novel. He commented on The Golden Lotus and The Carnal Prayer Mat, saying that they were works of punishing licentiousness, but he did not thoroughly understand Water Margin.

Wu Jianren's understanding of the society of novels and his critical attitude can be clearly seen from these words. He understood the importance of novels from a progressive feudal perspective, hoping to use them to change customs and transform society, and reform society. This is all the material about his theory of novels that can be found now.

Promoting Night Talk 220

Xu Ying

Carrying the cartwheel-sized setting sun on my back, I hurriedly rode my bicycle. As the last rays of the sun disappeared, and a few patches of sunset glow flickered in the clear sky, I arrived at Zhongyu's home. Entering the gate, I turned past the row of sunflower fences and saw the family eating in front of the eaves. I went in, disrupting their gathering.

"We thought you wouldn't make it back from the city—" Zhongyu stood up, saying with a hint of apology. His wife busily offered to fetch water for me to wash my face.

"Haha," I laughed, "Have I become a guest after only three days of moving out?"

At this moment, an old man with weathered skin, sitting at the head of the table, his head bandaged from a wound, interjected with a raspy voice and Zhongyu's local accent:

"My fault—my fault, I am sorry—"

This was Zhongyu's older brother, Boxian, who had fled here three days ago. He was temporarily staying in my room, so I had moved to Guan Di Temple to sleep on the floor. But I still ate meals with them every day. The family seemed to feel a bit guilty about this.

"You're too kind," I said, casually taking a newspaper from my pocket and handing it to him. "The news about your incident is on today's paper."

"What does it say?" Zhongyu's wife asked sharply.

Boxian took it with a dry, black hand, which was also wrapped in several pieces of tape. He only glanced at the headline – "Farmer Riot – Promoter Assaulted" – curled his nostrils, and handed it to Zhongyu without a word.

"Most people don't understand the suffering of promoters..." I continued.

Zhongyu and his wife huddled together, reading the news, intermittently making sounds, "What, promoters forced...", "The people are violent...", "Brother, – your office burned down?", "Ah, more than thirty people imprisoned," "Poor management, triggering – triggering a people's uprising..."

The haggard man silently picked up a cup of wine from the table and drained it in one gulp. A faint purplish-red color flushed over his dark face. I felt that I shouldn't have made the situation so tense, so I picked up the wine pot and refilled his cup, pouring one for myself as well. "Brother, please," I said, raising my cup in a toast.

Zhongyu also put down the newspaper to join in the joking. I reported a few pieces of news from the city, adding a few humorous remarks, and the atmosphere returned to normal, until we saw the stars in the sky.

Stars hung in the sky. The dining table became a tea table. In the center of the table, the kerosene lamp attracted green floating gnats, gray night moths, and shiny black beetles. Zhongyu suggested blowing out the lamp. In the darkness, we drank tea, Boxian's fingers tapping the teacup, seemingly playing a tune. A swarm of mosquitoes harmonized with a new melody. We each held a banana leaf fan, keeping "time." After a moment of silence, Zhongyu spoke.

"Brother, Mr. Li is here too, can you tell us how this promotion went?"

"It's pointless to talk about it," the raspy voice replied heavily in the darkness, "I won't scold the common people, and of course, I won't scold myself. To be honest, if it wasn't for food, who would do this?"

We listened quietly, the katydids chirping in the grass.

"This thing—let's call it a riot. I've been through it twice. That year in ××, it was promoting cotton. That self-growing cotton wasn't any better than the common people's local cotton, and the cotton bolls rotted easily, turning the cotton yellow. The first year we barely managed to plant it, and the first year there was a riot. This time, it's silkworm eggs. The silkworm eggs are good, they're good, but they go onto the mountains a week later than the common people's silkworm eggs. That week's mulberry leaves are the most terrifying to eat. That year, I watched mulberry leaves become gold, impossible to afford. Piles of silkworm babies were sent to the latrine. My heart ached for them too..."

Fireflies flitted through the sky. He coughed lightly.

"This year, the superiors sent down these silkworm eggs again. For the sake of food, I still have to promote them. I deserve to be beaten this time. The common people are not guilty at all. They are not for people to research. They have to pay taxes and complete their quotas. The whole family, old and young, depends on this for food and clothing. They are not guilty..."

We sighed together. To avoid making our friend suffer, we changed the subject.

Job Application (Continued to Completion) 221

— Li Huiying

The manager took out two cigars, handing one to Luo Fei. Luo Fei declined:

"Mr. Manager, I don't smoke."

"Really?" "Really."

"Ah, that's excellent."

The manager smoked his cigar, his eyes gazing absentmindedly at the smoke rings, then back at Luo Fei's face. After a while, he tapped off the ash and said:

"I think you're very good, good, I'll hire you. Come here at nine o'clock tomorrow to complete the procedures and officially start working. Miss Luo, don't forget this is my goodwill, only you were kept from more than twenty applicants."

Luo Fei thanked the manager for his goodwill and left.

Walking out of the ×× company's door, Luo Fei realized she was drenched in sweat. Fortunately, those meteor-like eyes were no longer revolving around her. She felt relieved and thought that Lu Wen must be waiting for her for a long time, so she hurried to the Jiangbian Pier, thinking: how should I tell him? Should I tell him about the manager's frivolousness? Lu Wen would be unhappy to hear it. Should I tell him I got the job? Of course, I should tell him, he'll be happy...

At the pier, she looked east and west, but couldn't find Lu Wen. There were many people, but he was nowhere to be seen. Anxious, she wanted to call out, but felt a little embarrassed, and she didn't have such a loud voice. After a long time, she couldn't find him and felt as if she had lost her heart. She anxiously blamed Lu Wen, complaining that he wasn't considerate enough. He should have come to meet her, like a victorious general welcomed by his lover.

Lu Wen walked over from the side. Luo Fei grabbed him and asked anxiously:

"Where did you go, Wen? I've been looking for you for a long time!"

"I met a friend and walked with him for a while. How did it go? Didn't work out, right?"

"On the contrary!"

"You mean? Hired?"

"Exactly."

Luo Fei could tell that Lu Wen didn't seem right, so she quickly asked:

"Wen, why aren't you happy? What are you thinking about?"

"I'm not thinking about anything."

"You're lying."

"Really, it's nothing, but I just feel that companies hiring female employees are mostly up to no good."

"It all depends on the person," Luo Fei smiled, trying to cheer Lu Wen up, "Is that right?"

"I hope so."

"Aren't you going to congratulate me?" Luo Fei changed the subject. "You should be happy."

Lu Wen did smile, and even jumped up and down.

"Of course, I should congratulate you. I'll buy you a thank-you gift later."

The two walked along the left side of the road on the sidewalk. They were walking home. Although they were a little tired, they now had a lot of energy. They looked very proud, and the sky seemed to deliberately shine brightly on their way forward.

"I forgot to ask you, when do you officially start working?" Lu Wen suddenly remembered. "When do you start?"

"Nine o'clock tomorrow."

"Tomorrow you will be a person with a profession."

"Tomorrow our lives will be a little more secure."

But Lu Wen thought about the "up to no good" thing again. Why did he have to think about that? He felt sad. He thought that his wife's job search was absolutely not a success of skill, but was actually similar to prostitution. However, keeping his wife at home as a good wife and mother was not his idea. He had always advocated that women should serve society just like men, and that women should do things just like men.

When there is no job, you are afraid of not finding one. When you have a job, you think about other issues. How contradictory.

Luo Fei was also recalling the moment in the manager's home. Thinking about it, she was a little worried about herself in the future. If the manager's frivolity continued, how could she deal with it? The retention of her job was also tied to his hands. As long as he was unhappy for a moment, she could be sacrificed. It seemed that she couldn't go against his wishes, but if that was the case, there would be more problems in the future. After thinking about it, she couldn't come up with a reliable solution. The final decision was still to do as she had told Lu Wen: It depends on the person. She added an explanation: stay if it fits, leave if it doesn't.

Lu Wen walked along and bought two packs of peanuts. He kept one pack for himself and handed the other pack to his wife, smiling:

"Fei, this is my gift to celebrate you."

"Too meager. Alright, a small gift with great meaning."

Luo Fei also smiled.

The Customs House clock pointed to twelve o'clock. The clerks of the company's banks took buses and trams to go home for meals, and some went to nearby restaurants to eat their fill. Every bus was very crowded, "One more in the back!" the ticket seller shouted loudly.

Lu Wen and Luo Fei were also a little hungry and wanted to hurry home to cook. After walking for a while, Lu Wen led his wife onto a bus. After they were seated, he said in a low voice:

"Anyway, we've found a job, let's join the fun."
