University Days (11) 223

— Written by the German Storm, translated by Chen Yinzi

On the Mill Pond

The New Year has passed. For a long time, I had been in love with my pair of smooth steel-bottomed Dutch skates, and I somewhat despised my classmates, because they only had those old rough iron-bottomed skates. But now the severe cold has arrived.

It was a Sunday afternoon a week. The Mill Pond, not far from the city, a lake of medium size, was covered with a layer of shimmering ice mirror. Half the city's residents gathered there, in the fresh winter air. Old and young, some wearing a pair of skates, some wearing only one skate, some even tying a cow bone to the bottom of their shoes, were practicing this noble sport of skating. Some tents were set up near the shore; nearby, on land, roaring stoves burned with steaming pots, and various warming beverages were supplied from the pots. Here or there, one could see a hand-pulled sled rushing from the crowd to the open ice, in the sled was a girl with a stern face, but everyone was still walking near the shore of the lake, the center of the lake did not seem to be completely safe.

I tied my steel skates to my feet and skated along the shore of the lake by myself. When I turned back, I saw that the dance partners had almost all gathered near the tents. The little girls were wearing winter coats, leaning forward slightly, walking tremblingly on the ice surface that seemed to have already formed tracks. Fritz had already put his yellow horn sled carved with a deer head in the mill the day before, and at this time he pushed Miss Lotte back, and another dance partner wearing a gorgeous tiger skin sat in the sled. This knight paused for a moment, looking around as if to find an assistant to help him with this not-so-easy job of serving the girls, but at this time I happened to turn my face away, because among the groups of working-class women and girls in front, I saw Rena Li · Bolijia; I had not met her since the last dance night. Those girls took turns calling a trainee—he was an apprentice of the carpenter who did business with my family—they pushed a light sled, and I immediately recognized that this snow-like thing belonged to my old friend Christopher. I also saw his sister, but he himself was not there. The brilliance of the ice mirror probably attracted him to the center of the lake, because among all the boys in the city, he was one of the best skaters.

Page 17

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Talking Points

The De Facto Nine-Power Treaty 224

— Jia Wei

The June 20 newspapers carried a report from the Tokyo branch of the Reuters news agency: "Regarding British Ambassador to the United States Lindsay's visit to the U.S. State Department on the 17th, a report from Washington stated that the United Kingdom and the United States want to form a common front, invoke the Nine-Power Treaty, and contain Japan's actions towards China. The UK, US, and Japan will take concrete actions, and the Japanese diplomatic authorities take a calm attitude towards this, believing it is not worthy of a knowledgeable person's smile... In the event that the United Kingdom and the United States join forces to invoke the Nine-Power Treaty and protest to Japan, it will resolutely reject it based on the following views: (1) The Hebei issue has been resolved by the parties concerned between China and Japan, and other countries cannot intervene; (2) The Nine-Power Treaty, which the United Kingdom and the United States often invoke, cannot be recognized as a backing for the United Kingdom and the United States to speak to Japan on the Hebei issue; (3) Japan believes that the treaty's effect has de facto disappeared after the Manchurian Incident."

From 1922 to now, there have been more than ten years of history for our grand "Nine-Power Treaty"; however, it has "de facto disappeared." Shouldn't the people involved take a deep breath after hearing this?

However, things are not accidental. Take the "League of Nations" for example. What is it "de facto"? This is also well known to "knowledgeable people"! Moreover, today's era, this world, seems too great. The complexity and change of all relationships are truly elusive. And "reality" is surging like a raging wave, not stopping for a moment.

Look; a shop with the golden sign of "One-Voice Hall" is hanging up colorful flags in the high sky every day with "Big Discount" and "Big Liquidation." It is said that "there is more than enough to cover both payments and receipts," but in the end, it announces "liquidation" and "closure." Natural disasters cause famine, and even a good harvest cannot make a living. You have a skill, but you don't have a place to use it... Even more like: on the one hand, some people are singing about "peaceful cooperation" and "calling for peace," on the other hand, everyone is implementing compulsory military service, rearming, building new ships, and expanding the air force... on the one hand, singing "national revival" and "peaceful construction"... everything is so contradictory, opposed, conflicting, and fighting—this is today's society, and also today's world!

Well, the "Nine-Power Treaty" has "de facto disappeared." And "facts" will tell us all the true masks!

Page 18

Old Man Chen, the Broker 225

— Qin Jian

(One of the Scenery and Customs series)

On a busy street, there is a small room. In the center of the room is a square table with faded paint. People often wash clothes and sew quilts on it, so the table has become pitifully dilapidated over the years. Two rows of benches are placed against the left and right walls. A "Statue of Emperor Xuanwu" hangs on the middle wall, and some red paper scraps with "No Taboos" are randomly pasted on both sides, along with those slogan-like red paper strips. "Friends and relatives, recommend without guarantee," "Taking office immediately, a successful arrow (recommendation)": outside the door, black characters are written on a red-painted sign: "Old Man Chen's Employment Agency."

Early in the morning, after opening the sliding door, "Old Man Chen, the Broker," is very noisy. There are those who live in the shop, and those who come from outside to "get business." There are young and old: there are "raw goods" who have just come out of the countryside, and "old hands" who "have been eating other people's food" for a long time: there are old women who recently lost their sons and daughters-in-law in the famine, carrying a sixty-year-old body, risking death to come to this metropolis to be employed, looking for a possibility of survival; and on the other hand, there are those who abandoned their newborns, taking advantage of this good opportunity, desperately entrusting people to bring them to Shanghai, planning to use their children's nutrition—these plump milk, to feed the "young masters" in the "mansions," in exchange for some money to pay the rent... These people are all filled with anxiety, hope, and excitement, expectantly sitting in rows on these benches, curiously looking at the outside world, the outside people, the outside streets, and in their hearts they think about the familiar countryside that is broken but intimate, the relatives who hanged themselves in the famine, their own babies who have been passed into the hands of others, the past peaceful days, the mysterious arrival of "business," the fast passing of days and nights, their own lives tomorrow...

(How unbelievable the outside world is! Those big houses, those cars, those gentlemen and ladies wearing "foreign clothes," those terribly scary restaurants and theaters... This world is really not bad! But why do we have to live through days of constant famine, handing our babies into the hands of others?)

This is a mystery, a mystery that is hard to imagine: "Maybe—no, really! Maybe with good luck, you can "get on" in a good mansion, work hard for years, and even earn a few coffin capital, right? Isn't it true that the Gen Sheng mother's family in Xiqiaotou in the countryside, both the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law have "helped" "people" in Shanghai for several years, and came back to build houses, redeem fields for graves, and live comfortably?"

However, as she thought, the old woman who did "rough work" sitting on the opposite bench seemed to have guessed people's fantasies? And she was about to give this dream a head-on blow, aiming at some people's beautiful empty calculations, and started talking.

——Hmph, do you think it's easy to eat other people's food on the Shanghai Bund? These days, "one place is barren, everywhere is barren." There are many people who come out to eat other people's food, and the families who hire people are just "picking the best and the fattest" to choose from. I've been in Shanghai for two or three months since Qingming, and I've been sitting in the broker's shop without anyone coming to see me. Finally, a mansion wanted an old nanny. I begged the shop to send people, and I promised him extra sending money. I went there to try it for three days. The superiors said: "The person is still capable, but the appearance is annoying, and the age is a little too old. We here want someone young and able to be seen in front of people." Think about it, isn't it annoying! I came back and was blamed by the sender, saying that I wasted their time, and they knew it was wrong. Think about it, we sell our strength, but we also have to sell our age, figure, and even our insides.

People all sank their hearts, as if even the "Old Man Chen, the Broker" large signboard outside the door was a little dusty.

Memories of Photography 226

— Hua

The year I graduated from county elementary school, my uncle gave me a camera as a souvenir. It was a very simple camera, much like the "box camera" on the market now, with a fixed-focus lens. You could take a good picture by pressing the shutter in the designated position. This sparked my interest in photography. During that summer vacation, I carried the camera everywhere, forcing my neighbors, uncles, and brothers to be captured in my lens. In the evening, I would pester my uncle to develop the film, using my father's study as a darkroom. Since there were no electric lights in the countryside, I made a red gauze lantern. When I worked in the dark, swarms of mosquitoes buzzed around, and I could almost touch a few small bodies with a wave of my hand. My uncle was particularly fond of me, and although he couldn't stand this unexpected sacrifice, he would pat my head and say repeatedly, "You're driving me crazy!" He would also provide detailed criticism of the developed photos, which naturally increased my courage. But the results at that time were really bad. Out of six negatives, I couldn't even vaguely recognize two of them as my uncles or brothers. I, however, was very excited. If it was a blurry shadow and my uncle asked me who it was, I would immediately tell him it was Uncle Dog from next door. "Who is taller than him?" I would argue as evidence. My father would always use these jokes as conversation material during dinner. But my interest only increased. When I was admitted to county middle school in the next semester, my uncle mailed me two books on "Introduction to Photography" from Shanghai, and I learned that the first step in photography should be to photograph still life. I already felt that the subjects of my photography were gradually decreasing, and the range of still life was naturally wider. The loquat tree in the backyard and my younger brother's "standing barrel" (a wooden device to prevent children from falling) were all captured by my lens. After a year of wasting countless negatives, my uncle would always pat my head and praise me as a photographic genius when he helped me develop the film, if he found a photo where the light, angle, and exposure showcased my photographic skills. He always guided me, pointing out the reasons for my failure in the bad photos. One year during spring break, I wanted to expand the scope of my photography, so I went to Hangzhou with my uncle. We took many pictures of the beautiful West Lake. Each picture was taken after Uncle Zhang had explained the scenery in detail. Almost every photo from that trip was satisfactory.

But after that, I lost interest in photography, which was a natural result. People often neglect food and drink to study something new, but after making some progress, they have already shifted their interest to another new thing. However, I carefully collected all those photos, arranged them in photo albums, and organized them chronologically. At the same time, I started collecting other people's photography. I bought photography collections of several famous photographers, as long as I knew about them. I remember once visiting the Black and White Society's photography exhibition. There were two photos with a price of twenty-five yuan each. I stood there blankly, not wanting to leave. When I got home, I was even willing to steal to get them, which shows my love for photography. Although I stopped studying it further after parting with the camera my uncle gave me.

This time, while moving, I found my treasured souvenirs in a broken box. Some of them were almost completely faded. When I opened the earliest album, it was completely a moldy piece of paper. I couldn't even recognize who the tall Uncle Dog from next door was. But I still carefully sorted them out and preserved them, hoping that one day I would suddenly remember them and review my old dreams. Childhood souvenirs are worth cherishing. They give me sweet memories and bitter sadness.

Chapters of Melancholy 227

— Xia Yin

(I) Depression

The melancholy of the century is impossible to dispel. Wanderers can only lonely sigh without coherent verses. Long strings of days drift by in the taste of melancholy.

Who can I confide in, this unspeakable hidden pain? The traces left by more than twenty years of life groping in the sea of people are just a series of loneliness, a series of oddities, a series of coldnesses: Can the bright smiles under the neon lights really fill the cracks in life? Alas, the jazz played by the Filipinos is just the trembling of professionals.

What a contradiction, no, how tired I am of these days of wandering idleness. The summer night streets with bright moon and neon lights, the ease and cheerfulness, are enough to bewitch people. But what is a wanderer walking there for?

I don't understand. What accompanies a wanderer is just a long string of gray dreams that never end. Tonight, I carry my own loneliness again, crawling as slowly as a snail through this street with bright moon and neon lights. All the quick rhythms, in my eyes, become a blur, making me dizzy and my heart tremble. However, I cannot leave it. I don't have the courage to put away the intoxication of this decadent urban style, to open up new, healthy land sufficient to settle my own thoughts, beliefs, and emotions. I can't stop or awaken the disillusionment with reality, the melancholy of the century woven into my life. So, I can only lonely utter sighs without coherent verses, considering it a curse for the weariness of a wandering life. And the strings of days drift by in the taste of melancholy.

How heartbreaking is this? When I quietly reflect in the still of the night, I can clearly discern a clear path for this decadent life. Isn't this akin to self-abandonment, tearing everything apart, letting strings of gray dreams corrode the blood and strength of life? At this time, besides raising my hand to beat my head, trying to gain some spiritual relief in the physical pain, my heart will shout out:

——Why can't I be more energetic!

However, the days pass like a long flowing river: This cry of reflection, doesn't it also drift far away with the water like a petal falling on the water? Looking back at the current life, how is it changing? Alas, the price of shame is these flushed cheeks.

The melancholy of the century is impossible to dispel, and long strings of days drift by in this taste of melancholy.

(II) Silence

Ever since I shouldered the burden of life, I have been like a bird that has lost its flock, disappearing the innocent songs: The bitter juice of life has gradually turned me into silence. Years of drifting, stumbling on the rugged road of life's storms, I have never received love, sympathy, or understanding from the world. Coldness, slander, and jealousy, like a wolf with fierce eyes, lurk around me at all times, jumping out from time to time to take a bite. Enduring the pain, I let the bright red blood flow under my feet, silently seeping into the mud. This endless suffering, the young heart, has gradually faded away the elegant sincerity: It has turned into silence, calmness, and uses silence to pass the years.

But before the journey of life is over, the burden of life cannot be put down, and the bitter juice of life will become even more bitter and intense: This endless suffering!

Odes to Rain 228

— Zhen

I never dreamed there would be such a warm clap of thunder.

But although that thunderclap clearly swept past Uncle Nanhai's ears, and the thatched hut, like a sleepy crane on the beach, shook, he still didn't believe it. When he fell asleep, the sky was clear and there wasn't a single cloud in sight, it couldn't have changed so quickly—

This was the answer of his two minds: on one hand celebrating the seasonable rain, on the other hand still doubting that heaven was still so stingy.

He jumped out of bed, and trembling, opened the door to look at the sky. The sky and him, one happy and one angry, formed a contrast: In the southwest corner of the sky, dark cloud peaks climbed upwards, gradually covering the azure face, obscuring the twinkling stars, as if a touch would cause countless sparks to burn this earth. He, his face wrinkled like a wild lily, was so happy that he had no proper words to comfort himself. He walked to the front of the bed and hit his old woman:

"Get up and see—there's food to eat!"

The old woman followed his hand and ran out, her ragged clothes snagging on her body: her seven- or eight-year-old son was even happier.

Page 19

Hearing that there was enough to eat, he had been eating vegetable porridge for almost a month and never had a full stomach. Hearing his father's words in a dream, he rolled out of bed, shouting:

"Dad, I want to eat!"

He thought his dad had brought rice or something else home in the middle of the night.

He stumbled in the dark house, and the jars made a clear sound. The old woman quickly felt her way in, scolding her son:

"You little troublemaker, what are you eating in the middle of the night!"

"Didn't Dad say there's enough to eat?" the son argued.

"It's going to rain. When it rains, we harvest the grain and then we have food to eat. After eating a full meal, you have to sleep! Understand?" She helped her son up.

"Mom! I'm hungry." The son choked out a sob.

"Go to sleep! You won't feel hungry when you're asleep."

"The hungrier I am, the harder it is to sleep!"

Seeing that the son didn't go to sleep, he followed his mother outside to look at the sky. The sky was spitting out water, and there was a faint breeze and a stuffy heat.

"Don't blow wind; let it rain more. Bodhisattva, if it dries up again, we won't be able to live!" Uncle Nanhai murmured, like talking to himself, with one hand on his son's head.

The son smelled the warm wind, although it didn't reduce his hunger at all, but thinking about the white rice, the live crucian carp in the future, a drop of saliva oozed out of his mouth. (To be continued)

Lianhua Establishes Drama Troupe 232

The drama troupe of Lianhua Music and Drama Group held a preparatory meeting a few days ago, and elected 21 preparatory committee members, including Sun Yu, Fei Mu, Jin Yan, Zheng Junli, Chen Yanyan, Wang Renmei, Li Lili, and Diao Banhua. The group is divided into five sections: directing, script, general affairs, administrative affairs, and stage affairs. It is scheduled to select a script within a few days and start rehearsals immediately, and plans to hold the first public performance on September 1.

Shanghai Opera Society 233

Will Hold Public Performances; Officially Recruiting Members

The Shanghai Opera Society, led by Yan Hua and Liu Hengzhi, has officially started recruiting members. Those who are interested in singing, dancing, and drama arts can go to No. 19 Qingdao Road, Shanghai to get an application form (please attach 2 cents for postage when mailing). It is reported that the society plans to provide considerable training to the members recruited this time. Once the training is mature, they will be allowed to contribute to the art of opera on a large scale on the stage.

Lianhua Vignettes 234

There are four Han Langens in "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp"; but these four Han Langens are not played by one person.

Lin Chuchu plays an old, dizzy woman in "Tianlun". Her posture of threading a needle and sewing is lifelike.

Luo Peng's recent work "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River" is the first major drama since he joined Lianhua.

The script being written by Cai Chusheng depicts the wandering life of children in a very profound way. The power of the ending and the novelty of its form are unprecedented in Chinese films.

Ma Xu Weibang, the director of "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River," recently lost a front tooth. Ma Xu said to people: "This is great, it saves me from having to put on makeup for old people's plays"!

For one shot in "Tianlun," a wooden platform five feet high, eight feet wide, and dozens of feet long was built, looking like a giant bridge. A large group of children walked in formation neatly and solemnly on the platform. Looking at it, the background was floating clouds, the shadows of people moved, and the camera followed, it was truly a spectacle.

"Triumphal Song" and "Humanity" 235

"Humanity," which caused a sensation in the film industry in those years, depicted the tragic struggles of the people in the northwest during the early disaster. Now, Yihua is producing a sound film called "Triumphal Song," which is also a story about the suffering of people in the drought. The directors of both films are Mr. Bu Wancang, one of the most famous directors in the Chinese film industry.

Although the theme of "Triumphal Song" and "Humanity" is the same, the plot is completely different. At the same time, the consciousness of "Triumphal Song" is more correct, and the story is more tragic and touching than "Humanity."

Obviously, Bu Wancang created new techniques in "Humanity" that were not available in domestic films at the time. Judging from Bu Wancang's special efforts in the work of "Triumphal Song," "Triumphal Song" will also have new and excellent techniques for us to see.

Yihua Sound Film "The Storm" 236

"Big Family" Passes Review Again 237

"Big Family," directed by Zhang Shichuan and starring all the male and female actors of Mingxing Film Company, has passed the re-examination a few days ago.

"Big Family" depicts the tragedy of a gentry family crushed by the cruel wheels of the times, while highlighting the phenomenon of rural bankruptcy and the sins of prosperous cities. Like a mirror of the times, it reflects all kinds of joys and sorrows in life. It is no exaggeration to say that it can help people to further understand the entire organization of modern society.

Zhang Shichuan's films are famous for their large scenes, and this one is no exception, with many of the great sets in "Cecil B. DeMille's" works.

In order to meet people from all walks of life as soon as possible, the entire staff of "Big Family" has been working almost day and night these days. It is expected that we will be able to meet smoothly soon.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Automobile Weekly

Calibration of Automobile Engine Ignition Timing 238

— Chen Xing

——Commonly known as "Setting the Timing"——

Most automobile engines are four-stroke cycle engines. That is, the crankshaft rotates twice, and the pistons in each cylinder move up and down twice, completing the four strokes of intake, compression, explosion, and exhaust. Therefore, regardless of the number of cylinders in the engine, each cylinder explodes once every two revolutions of the crankshaft to produce power. However, the explosion timing of each cylinder must be fixed; it cannot be too early or too late. Furthermore, the order of these explosions, that is, the engine's firing order, must strictly adhere to the regulations and cannot be disturbed in the slightest. Only in this way can the engine's operation be perfected.

Fuel is drawn into the cylinder, compressed, and then ignited and exploded by an electric spark from the ignition system. Therefore, the timing of this spark and the sequence of its occurrence in each cylinder have a direct relationship to the explosion timing of each cylinder and the engine's firing order. Thus, it is necessary to rigorously align them. Performing this task is known as calibrating the engine's ignition timing.

When performing calibration, the piston of the first cylinder (the one closest to the radiator, hereinafter the same) must first be placed at the top dead center of the compression stroke. The different methods are described below.

(1) Remove the spark plug from the first cylinder, and press your thumb against the opening of its installation hole. Then, turn the crankshaft with the hand crank. When you feel pressure pushing upwards on your finger, the cylinder is in the compression stroke and the piston is moving upwards. At this point, remove your finger and insert a bent wire through the opening. At the same time, continue to slowly turn the crankshaft. Determine the point where the piston can no longer move upwards, and you can then conclude that it has reached top dead center.

(2) If the intake and exhaust valves can be seen after removing the spark plug, then whether the cylinder is in the compression stroke can also be visually determined. When the crankshaft is turned, observe the intake valve of the first cylinder (in inline engines, the two at both ends are exhaust valves, and the intake and exhaust valves in the middle alternate). The intake valve opens and then closes (i.e., rises to the top and then goes down), which indicates the beginning of the compression stroke. Whether the piston has reached the top can be determined using a bent wire, as described above.

(3) By feeling the valve tappet of the last cylinder (near the flywheel housing), you can also determine whether the piston of the first cylinder is at the top dead center of the compression stroke. Slowly turn the crankshaft until the exhaust valve of the last cylinder opens and then closes (i.e., the last valve tappet rises to the top and then descends). Then, continue to slowly turn the crankshaft, and rotate the valve tappets by hand. If the exhaust valve tappet can only be turned with difficulty, while the intake valve tappet can still be turned freely, then the piston of the last cylinder is at the top dead center of the exhaust stroke. In inline engines, the pistons of the first and last cylinders are generally on the same plane. Since the piston of the last cylinder has completed its exhaust stroke, the piston of the first cylinder must undoubtedly be at the top dead center of its compression stroke.

(4) If the cylinder head is removed, it is simpler. You can turn the crankshaft with the hand crank until the intake valve of the first cylinder opens and then closes tightly. Continue to turn the crankshaft until the piston reaches top dead center.

(5) The above methods are applicable to engines with overhead valves. For engines with inverted valves, the valve rocker cover can be removed. Then, turn the crankshaft, observing the intake valve of the first cylinder. It opens and then closes again. Then, feel the gap between the valve rocker arm and the valve stem. If the gaps for both intake and exhaust valves are similar, then the piston of the first cylinder can be determined to be at the top dead center of its compression stroke.

(6) For engines with special markings, alignment with the markings can be more accurate. For example, last year's Buick cars had inverted valves. A small hole was set on the side of the flywheel housing, covered with a movable small door. Two straight lines were horizontally engraved on either side of the hole, and a straight line was also horizontally engraved on the flywheel, with the letters "ADY" marked above it. Rotate the crankshaft until the exhaust valve of the third cylinder (i.e., the fifth valve counting backwards from the radiator) has opened. Then, continue to slowly rotate it until the straight lines on the flywheel and flywheel housing are completely aligned. At this point, the piston of the first cylinder has reached the top dead center of its compression stroke.

Once the position of the first cylinder's piston has been determined, it must not be moved again. The spark plug can then be reinstalled. Next, remove the distributor cap and loosen the locking screw on the distributor housing or the eccentric. If this locking screw is for locking the housing, it will be exposed externally. Once loosened, the housing can be rotated freely. If it is for locking the eccentric, the distributor brush must be removed, the locking screw loosened and removed. Then, place the distributor brush back on so that the eccentric can be rotated. Then, rotate the housing or distributor brush to ensure that the fiber piece on the points is being lifted by the eccentric, and the points are fully open. The contact on the distributor brush is pointing to a contact point on the distributor cap. This contact point is not fixed. However, for ease of remembering, the usual practice is to always use the contact point aligned with the notch or tab specially provided on the edge of the distributor cap as the standard. Therefore, to make the distributor brush contact point point to the standard contact point on the distributor cap, there is no need to install the distributor cap when rotating the housing or eccentric. Simply ensure that the distributor brush contact point is aligned with the tab or notch specially provided on the edge of the housing (when the distributor cap is installed, the notch or tab on the cap will match this tab or notch). After aligning in this way, the locking screw can be tightened, and the distributor brush and distributor must be reinstalled as they were originally.

When the points are fully open, the gap must be appropriate; it cannot be too large or too small. If there is an abnormality, it should be recalibrated. First, loosen the locking screw on the points with a points wrench. Then, turn the adjustment screw slightly inwards or outwards to obtain a larger or smaller gap. Then, tighten it. The normal gap is approximately twelve to twenty-five thousandths of an inch. To know the exact number, it can be measured with a feeler gauge. If there is no feeler gauge, newspaper can be used instead. The thickness of one layer of newspaper is approximately five thousandths of an inch.

Then, connect the wire from the distributor cap that is aligned with the notch or tab (this wire is installed inside the wire head protector on the cap and is connected to the contact on the distributor brush) to the spark plug of the first cylinder. The remaining wires, according to the direction of rotation of the eccentric, connect the second and third wires in order to the spark plugs of each cylinder according to the engine's specified firing order. For example, if the firing order of a four-cylinder engine is 1-3-4-2, then the second wire should be connected to the third cylinder, the third wire should be connected to the fourth cylinder, and the fourth wire should be connected to the second cylinder. The same principle applies to six-cylinder engines.

The firing order for four-cylinder engines is 1-2-4-3 or 1-3-4-2. For six-cylinder engines, it is 1-5-3-6-2-4 and 1-4-2-6-3-5. The latter is only adopted by older workshops. However, most automobiles use the former. It is best to determine and remember this firing order before disassembly (regardless of the number of cylinders, knowing the direction of rotation of the distributor eccentric makes it easy to determine the wiring connecting the distributor cap to the spark plugs). Otherwise, the crankshaft can be turned to observe the order in which the intake and exhaust valves of each cylinder open. Or, remove all the spark plugs and press your finger or a wad of paper against the opening to test the order in which each cylinder compresses to determine it.

After calibrating in this way, the engine can be started to test it. If the timing of the spark supplied by the ignition system to each cylinder is too early or too late (commonly called "advanced" or "retarded"), it should be recalibrated. If it is too early, the car will jerk when starting. If it is too late, the engine will make a "pop pop pop" sound, and the car will be weak and slow. When recalibrating, the locking screws must still be loosened. Rotate the distributor housing or the eccentric a little to make the eccentric lift the fiber piece and open the points slightly earlier or later to obtain the correct timing. Regardless of whether the housing or eccentric is rotated, rotating in the direction of rotation retards the timing, and rotating against the direction of rotation advances the timing.

During operation, the timing of the spark supply must be advanced as the engine speed increases. This is because it allows the compressed fuel to explode completely when the piston reaches the top dead center, thereby reducing power loss. The amount of advance varies slightly for each car, but the maximum is approximately thirty degrees. For example, the maximum advance for a Ford Model B is twenty-nine degrees, for a V-8 06" (V-type eight-cylinder with a 106-inch wheelbase) it is twenty degrees, and for a V-8 r2" it is twenty-six degrees. Older cars have a spark lever installed on the dashboard or steering wheel to manage the timing. When the engine speed increases, this lever must be moved slightly in the direction of advance. However, most cars produced in recent years are automatically adjusted and do not require additional attention. If there is the former device installed on a car, the spark lever must be placed in the latest position when calibrating the ignition timing; there must be no mistake.

If the engine's ignition timing is not properly calibrated, it can cause the engine to malfunction, reduce power, over-consume fuel, generate excessive heat, and cause the car to jerk, damaging the components. If this situation occurs, strict correction must be made according to the above method. Only then will you avoid unexpected losses to your car.

Note: Diesel vehicles use the high heat generated by compressing air to cause the fuel to explode. Therefore, this article only applies to gasoline vehicles and does not apply to diesel vehicles.

An Indian Car Owner's Praise for a Mr. Morris Cowley 239

— Fu

Mr. Folana, an engineer residing in Gwalior, Central India, purchased a 1925 Morris Cowley two-seater used car that had been owned by four previous owners four years ago. Mr. Fo has recently written an article praising the car's unexpectedly good performance since he began using it. The article is as follows:

Based on the reports of the previous four car owners, I believe that this car had already traveled 50,000 to 60,000 miles before I purchased it. After I took possession of it, I inspected it in detail and found that all parts of the car were original and had not undergone any major repairs. After removing carbon deposits from the valves, regrinding them, and calibrating the carburetor, the car achieved over thirty miles per gallon of gasoline. Later, the gasoline mileage even reached thirty-five miles per gallon and has remained unchanged to this day. Since I purchased the car, I estimate that it has traveled over 200,000 miles. The routes traveled were mostly in the worst road conditions in Central India. What is particularly noteworthy is that during this period, the valves have only been ground twice and the bearings calibrated twice. Due to my work, I often drive over 300 miles a day, but no breakdowns have ever occurred along the way. This is especially rare and valuable. I am particularly proud of such a high-quality Morris vehicle. (Fu)

Results of South African Test of a Ten-Horsepower British Ford 240

Recently, the Cape Town office initiated a fourteen-day endurance test using a new top-of-the-line coupé (i.e., the "C" type, ten-horsepower British Ford). This car was equipped with standard equipment, with the exception of the 25-gallon gasoline tank and fog lights, which were extra fittings.

This car continued to run day and night without stopping. Each week, the circuit measured 112 miles, driven by five drivers taking turns. Fifty percent of the circuit was asphalt road, and the remainder was corrugated gravel pavement, including a mountain road section.

The car stopped every twenty-two hours to refuel and change the lubricant. High-pressure lubrication was applied every 1,000 miles. There were only two stops due to malfunctions. "One was due to a small puncture in the tire, and the other was to clear the fuel pump and remove lint. This lint was due to the lack of a filter between the auxiliary fuel tank and the pump. This would not have happened if the car had used the standard fuel tank.

That afternoon, the car completed its ninetieth circuit, traveling a total of 10,055 miles. The average speed, including all stops, was thirty miles per hour. The gasoline consumption was 39.97 miles per gallon. Less than half a gallon of oil was used, and thirteen pints of water.

This test was supervised by the automotive columnists of the "Cape Times" and the "Cape Argus." The two newspapers also appointed a committee of ten independent supervisors and auditors.

Seals were placed on all major parts of the car. Only one seal was broken to clear the gasoline pump. The car ran perfectly and was even better at the end of the test than at the beginning.

This car was a new car, randomly selected from the inventory held by the Ford Motor Company of South Africa in Elizabeth Port. It was driven for twelve hours before the test.

The drivers were amazed by the engine's performance. Even when passing through mountain roads, the engine never felt strained.

The car encountered various climatic conditions along the way. For most of the time, the car drove against the southeast wind, sometimes with wind speeds reaching eighty-six miles per hour. On some days, the temperature reached one hundred degrees. There were also two days of heavy rain.

The water temperature in the radiator was between ninety and ninety-five degrees, and the oil pressure remained constant at thirty-five pounds during the test.

Car News Briefs 241

— Yu

Increased Car Tax Revenue in the United States Last Year According to a recent survey by the American Automobile Association, special taxes levied on car owners in the United States by the federal, provincial, and local governments reached a record high in 1934. The total amount of motor taxes in 1934 was US$1,160,564,380. The figure for 1933 was US$1,128,262,331. A comparison of the two shows the difference. The breakdown of these taxes is as follows: provincial, county, and city combined, $898,226,722; federal, $262,337,558. Although provincial registration fees have decreased slightly, the increase in federal and provincial gasoline and personal property taxes has offset this. Thomas Henry, president of the American Automobile Association, said that this tax record should serve as a warning to provincial legislatures that are currently trying to increase tax rates. He also hopes that Congress will abolish the federal special tax on highway transportation.

Regulations on Used Car Advertising in the United States In the Detroit area of the United States, the sale of used cars is now subject to advertising restrictions. The American Better Business Bureau has established a standard of ethics. With the help of reputable car dealers and the cooperation of various newspapers, seductive and unethical advertisements are being rejected. Several terms and phrases are prohibited from being used. Therefore, in advertisements for the sale of used cars, phrases or words such as "perfect" and "like new" are strictly prohibited. The term "reconditioned" is also too vague. For example, any kind of repair on the car, from tightening a screw to cleaning a spark plug, can be described by this term. This method makes it easy to deceive car buyers and is therefore also prohibited. One rule that must be followed is that whenever a used car is sold, the year of manufacture and the body style must be stated in the advertisement. Using the phrase "free trial" to lure car buyers is also not allowed. The amount and timing of payments must be clearly stated without any ambiguity.

U.S. Military Orders Cars from Chevrolet Last year, Chevrolet produced more passenger cars than any other manufacturer. In 1934, the number of Chevrolet cars registered, including passenger cars and trucks, totaled 692,413, an increase of 118,040 compared to 1933. If passenger cars and trucks are counted separately, then passenger cars increased by 60,413, and trucks increased by 57,627. Recently, Chevrolet received a large order from the U.S. military for 2,200 trucks and 520 ambulances, with a total value of US$2,540,071.00.

British Austin Seven Speed Record Bertie Denly, who drove an Austin Seven in the Brooklands hill climb, recently set the International Class "I" record on the same track. The kilometer and mile records were 77.43 miles per hour and 85.95 miles per hour, respectively. This record is two miles per hour faster than the previous record set by Ivor Halet's "Emchee" small car. According to Tellis Valley, the Austin's performance was perfect that day, even though the weather was not very good. The original seven-horsepower Austin car was created in 1910, twenty-five years ago. The design of this earliest car, a two-seater open model, is very different from the current Austin Seven. The current four-seater is more comfortable, with air cushions, safety glass, and a flexible four-cylinder engine. Every feature is the latest. The progress of the past twenty-five years is truly amazing.

Dunlop Car Tire Launch Dunlop car tires are of high quality and are widely sold because they have oak fields and weaving mills. The raw materials are produced and managed by themselves, and improvements and manufacturing are greatly facilitated. They have oak fields in Malaya and textile mills in Lancaster's Lockdale, so the rubber and cotton produced are perfect. The products created are naturally extraordinary. The new "Ninety" tire is made from these excellent raw materials. When in use, it is naturally superior to others. This new tire is not only durable but also excels in anti-skid, firmness, and quietness.

Morris Sales Increase In January of this year, the sales of British Morris cars reached as many as 10,000 units. From this number, we can believe that Morris will soon set a new British car production record. According to Mr. Laut, chairman of the company, car production has continued to increase every week since last December. Therefore, it is obvious that a new record will be set in the near future. While Morris cars are selling well, the Cowley factory will not only spend £30,000 to renovate its interior but will also expand its factory base by one and a half acres.
